# Initial review

<details>
<summary>Config Constant Importance via Surrogate Modeling</summary>

## 1. Context and Motivation

### 1.2 What Issue \#5 Is Asking

> "By small model for working with bool, int, or float constants in the config figure out existing parameters importance."

Concretely:
- Build a lightweight model that operates **only on config constants** (primarily `[CLASSIFY]` and `[TEXT_UTILS]`).
- Experiment with new values for those constants and evaluate their impact on existing line categories.
- Treat the input directory of per-line CSVs as **immutable ground truth**; write any re-categorizations to a **separate output directory**.
- Report which parameters are **most responsible** for category assignments — so high-importance constants can be prioritized for manual tuning and low-importance ones can be safely hardcoded.

### 1.3 Why a Surrogate Approach Is Necessary

Executing the full GPU pipeline — which requires Qwen2.5-0.5B inference over massive XML repositories plus FastText language identification — is computationally prohibitive for exhaustive parameter sweeps. Traditional Grid Search or Monte Carlo simulation over 22 interacting parameters is mathematically intractable at this scale.

The key architectural insight is that the per-line feature CSVs already contain **every expensive signal pre-computed**: `perplex`, `lang_score`, `garbage_density`, `word_weird`, `vowel_ratio`, `rot_ratio`, etc. Recategorization from those CSVs requires only cheap arithmetic — no GPU, no model calls. This makes parameter sensitivity analysis tractable on a laptop.

---

## 2. Pipeline Architecture

### 2.1 ALTO Extraction

The pipeline parses ALTO XML files using three extraction protocols prioritized by document complexity:

| Protocol | Profile | Mechanism |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **LayoutReader** | Moderate compute | Primary method. Reconstructs logical reading order from spatial bounding boxes; handles hyphenated words split across line breaks. |
| **alto-tools** | High speed, CPU-bound | Direct XML element parsing without spatial reconstruction. Optimal for linear layouts. |
| **GLM (LLM-based)** | High compute, GPU-bound | Patched GLM-4v-9b visual language model; reserved for severely degraded or highly irregular layouts. |

### 2.2 Asymmetric CPU/GPU Processing Architecture

Following extraction, text undergoes quality assessment in an asymmetric CPU/GPU pipeline:

- **One GPU worker** hosts Qwen2.5-0.5B exclusively for perplexity scoring. Perplexity serves as a proxy for linguistic coherence — garbled OCR naturally produces anomalously high perplexity.
- **Up to 32 CPU workers** handle file I/O, FastText language identification, structural detection heuristics, and a shared queue feeding text batches to the GPU. Workers continuously poll the result dictionary in a non-blocking asynchronous loop.

This design prevents OOM errors and hardware bottlenecking. The pipeline is entirely vectorized over pre-computed features when operating from CSVs in re-categorization mode.

### 2.3 Categorization Logic

The pipeline produces a ten-signal composite `quality_score` in `[0.0, 1.0]` via `compute_quality_score`, then assigns each line a category via `categorize_line`:

| Category | Status | Description |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Clear** | Preserved | Passes all structural heuristics with high composite score. Ready for downstream NLP. |
| **Noisy** | Preserved (flagged) | Moderate degradation (fused tokens, anomalous capitalization, mildly elevated perplexity). Requires automated correction. |
| **Trash** | Discarded | Severe corruption: below quality thresholds or triggering override rules (all-caps, inverted-scan pages). |
| **Non-text** | Filtered | Too short, too few unique symbols, <30% alphabetic characters, or archival alphanumeric codes. |
| **Empty** | Ignored | Whitespace-only lines. |

---

## 3. The Configuration Space

### 3.1 Parameter Inventory

The 22 tunable constants in `config_langID.txt` / `text_util_langID.py` fall into five functional groups:

| Group | Constants | Role |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **QS weights** (10) | `QS_WEIGHT_VALID_WORD`, `_SYMBOL`, `_WEIRD`, `_PERPLEXITY`, `_LENGTH`, `_GARBAGE`, `_VOWEL`, `_LANG`, `_GIBBERISH`, `_FUSED` | Weighted sum that produces `quality_score`; normalized by `total_weight = sum(QS_WEIGHT_*)` |
| **Score thresholds** (3) | `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` (0.50), `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` (0.90), `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` (0.35) | Direct bucket boundaries in `categorize_line` |
| **Rotation / inversion gates** (2) | `ROT_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` (0.55), `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` (0.35) | Trigger `rot_penalty` subtraction in `compute_quality_score` |
| **Clean-prose fast-path** (5) | `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE` (0.65), `CLEAN_PROSE_WEIRD_MAX` (0.08), `CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX` (400.0), `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN` (4), `PPL_INVERTED_MIN` (200.0) | Sub-conditions gating Noisy→Clear promotion |
| **PPL normalization** (2) | `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` (1000.0), `SHORT_PPL_CAP` (850.0) | Cap raw perplexity before it enters `norm_ppl` |

### 3.2 Key Non-Linear Interactions and Vulnerabilities

The configuration space is deeply non-linear and prone to unintended cross-parameter consequences:

**Rotation detection pair**: `ROT_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` (minimum fraction of structurally rotatable characters such as `p`, `b`, `q`, `d`, `n`, `u`) is tightly coupled with `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` (minimum mean per-word weirdness required to confirm an upside-down page). Without the secondary parameter, legitimate Czech sentences with naturally high densities of rotatable letters could be falsely penalized.

**Clean-prose promotion chain**: `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE` sets a lower quality-score floor for Noisy→Clear promotion, but is gated by `CLEAN_PROSE_WEIRD_MAX` (a single severely corrupted token disqualifies the entire line) and `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN` (lines below this word count are excluded from perplexity-based promotion on statistical-reliability grounds).

**Perplexity coupling**: `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` anchors the `norm_ppl` denominator, so adjusting it rescales the contribution of every perplexity-related signal simultaneously. `SHORT_PPL_CAP` must remain below `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` — violating this constraint produces undefined normalization behavior.

**QS weight covariance**: The 10 `QS_WEIGHT_*` constants are not independent — `compute_quality_score` divides by `total_weight = sum(QS_WEIGHT_*)`. Changing one weight changes all normalized contributions. Standard importance methods will over-decompose into interaction terms unless this constraint is handled explicitly (see §5.3).

**Language threshold hierarchy**: `LANG_SCORE_ROUGH` (default 0.45) gates whether FastText predictions are trusted at all. `LANG_SCORE_CLEAR` (default 0.75) is the floor retroactively assigned to lines force-remapped to the collection default language. `TRUSTED_FOREIGN_LANGS` specifies languages that must never be remapped — e.g., Latin citations within Czech archaeological reports. This creates a conditional parameter space where some constants are entirely irrelevant if parent conditions are never triggered.

---

## 4. Theoretical Framework: Surrogate Modeling

### 4.1 What a Surrogate Model Is

A surrogate model (also called a meta-model or emulator) is a statistically lightweight approximation of a complex, expensive black-box function. In this context:

- The **true function** accepts a configuration vector (values for all 22 constants) and returns a performance metric (e.g., fraction of lines whose category changes vs. baseline).
- Evaluating the true function, even from CSVs, requires iterating over potentially millions of lines per trial.
- A **surrogate** is trained on a limited set of evaluated configuration points and maps the relationships between configuration inputs and performance outputs — enabling rapid prediction of untested configurations in sub-millisecond time.

### 4.2 Surrogate Architecture Selection

| Architecture | Profile | Applicability |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Gaussian Process Regression (GPR)** | Probabilistic, spatial | Provides uncertainty estimates but scales cubically with training samples and assumes continuous spaces; struggles with integer thresholds and boolean flags. |
| **Random Forest (RF)** | Ensemble, tree-based | Naturally handles non-linear interactions, categorical variables, and unscaled numerical data. Provides the algorithmic foundation for fANOVA variance decomposition via exact tree traversal. **Recommended primary surrogate.** |
| **Gradient Boosting (XGBoost)** | Ensemble, sequential | Superior at capturing sharp, discontinuous threshold effects (common in rule engines). Pairs well with SHAP for local explanation. Suitable as a secondary surrogate. |
| **Multilayer Perceptron (MLP)** | Neural network | Theoretically capable of approximating any function but requires large datasets to avoid overfitting and operates as an opaque black box — incompatible with interpretability requirements here. |

Given the mixed discrete/continuous space — float confidence bounds, integer word counts, boolean toggles, and hard rule thresholds — an ensemble tree-based surrogate is the mathematically optimal choice. These models require no input standardization and naturally approximate the step-like performance changes that occur when a hard filtering rule is marginally exceeded.

---

## 5. Hyperparameter Importance (HPI) Methodologies

### 5.1 Functional ANOVA (fANOVA)

fANOVA decomposes the variance of the trained surrogate into additive, orthogonal components that isolate the main effect of each individual parameter from higher-order interaction effects. For a Random Forest surrogate, these integrals are computed exactly by traversing node structures and leaf weightings — no Monte Carlo estimation required.

The output is a percentage: how much of the total performance variance is explained by each configuration constant. This enables precise statements such as "CLEAN\_PROSE\_MIN\_SCORE explains 34% of variance in category flip rate" and "it exhibits significant synergy with CLEAN\_PROSE\_WEIRD\_MAX."

Available via `optuna.importance.FanovaImportanceEvaluator` (recommended) or the standalone `fanova` library.

### 5.2 Shapley Additive Explanations (SHAP)

SHAP, derived from cooperative game theory, computes the marginal contribution of each parameter by evaluating the surrogate both with and without that parameter across all possible permutations of the others. Applied to a Random Forest or XGBoost surrogate, SHAP reveals non-linear threshold behaviors that global variance metrics may obscure.

For example, a SHAP dependency plot could reveal that increasing `LANG_SCORE_ROUGH` steadily improves categorization accuracy up to a specific inflection point, beyond which it begins aggressively miscategorizing archaic texts as Trash — a directional insight invisible to fANOVA's variance decomposition.

Available via `optuna.importance.ShapleyImportanceEvaluator` or the `shap` library directly.

### 5.3 Conditional PED-ANOVA

Standard fANOVA struggles with conditional parameter spaces where some constants are only relevant when parent conditions are triggered (e.g., `PPL_INVERTED_MIN` only affects the `rot_penalty` path; `TRUSTED_FOREIGN_LANGS` is irrelevant if `LANG_SCORE_ROUGH` is never failed). Conditional PED-ANOVA addresses this by estimating importance strictly within the top-performing configuration subset, computing divergence between global and optimal-region probability densities. This is particularly potent for rule-engine pipelines and avoids confounding importances with inactive logical branches.

For an initial sweep with 300–500 trials, standard fANOVA is sufficient. Conditional PED-ANOVA becomes valuable in Stage 2 once the conditional structure of the space is better understood.

### 5.4 Permutation Importance and Sobol Indices

Permutation Feature Importance measures the drop in surrogate predictive accuracy when a parameter's values are shuffled. It is computationally lightweight but has a known bias toward over-estimating importance of correlated features — a significant concern here given the strong covariance among QS weights. **Not recommended as the primary method**, but useful as a sanity check.

Sobol indices provide global sensitivity analysis conceptually identical to fANOVA but via computationally expensive Monte Carlo sampling rather than exact tree traversal. The SALib library provides both Morris (fast screening) and Sobol (full variance decomposition) implementations. Use Morris as a cheap pre-screen if the 22-parameter space needs further narrowing before the main sweep.

---

## 6. Recommended Implementation: Three-Layer Approach

### Layer 1 — `recategorize_from_csv.py` (Black-Box Evaluator)

This is the foundation: a **pure-Python re-scorer** that reads existing per-line feature CSVs and replays `compute_quality_score` + `categorize_line` with a given set of constants, without touching the input files.

**Interface:**
```bash
python tools/recategorize_from_csv.py \
    --input_dir  data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG \
    --output_dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG_recat \
    --config     config_langID.txt \
    [--override CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX=0.45 CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX=350.0 ...]
```

**Required CSV columns** (all already stored by `langID_classify.py`):
`lang_score`, `perplex`, `word_count`, `char_count`, `garbage_density`, `symbol`, `word_weird`, `vowel_ratio`, `gibberish`, `ldl_fuses`, `rot_ratio`, `text`

**Outputs:**
- Per-file and aggregated confusion matrices vs. original `categ` column
- Summary dict: `{categ: count}` and `flip_count` vs. baseline
- Revised CSVs with original columns preserved plus updated `quality_score` / `categ`

**Critical implementation constraint**: `compute_quality_score` reads module-level globals (`QS_WEIGHT_VALID_WORD`, etc.) loaded at import time. For the sweep to work without process-level isolation, factor out a `compute_quality_score_parametric(row, constants: dict) -> float` function in `text_util_langID.py` (or inline in `recategorize_from_csv.py`) that accepts constants as explicit arguments instead of reading globals. This is the cleanest option and avoids the monkey-patching overhead of `importlib.reload` per trial.

Follow the existing `langID_aggregate_STAT.py` file-I/O conventions: `glob("*.csv")`, per-file processing, `pathlib` throughout.

### Layer 2 — `const_importance_sweep.py` (Surrogate + fANOVA)

Wraps the evaluator as an Optuna objective and runs variance decomposition.

**Core loop:**
```python
for trial in optuna_study(sampler=RandomSampler(), n_trials=400):
    constants = {
        "CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX":  trial.suggest_float(...),
        "CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX":  trial.suggest_float(...),
        "CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX":    trial.suggest_float(...),
        "CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN":     trial.suggest_int(...),
        # ... all 22 constants
    }
    result = recategorize_from_csv(input_dir, constants=constants)
    return result["flip_rate"]   # objective

importances = optuna.importance.get_param_importances(
    study,
    evaluator=FanovaImportanceEvaluator(n_trees=64, seed=42)
)
```

**Outputs saved:**
- `param_importance.json` — normalized importance per constant
- `best_config.json` — constants at minimum flip_rate
- `pd_plots/top_pairs.png` — partial dependence plots for top-5 pairs

Dump study to SQLite (`storage="sqlite:///sweep.db"`) for persistence and resumption.

### Layer 3 — Targeted Local Refinement

Once the importance ranking is stable, narrow the search to the top-5 constants and run a short focused optimization (Optuna TPE or `skopt.forest_minimize`) in the reduced subspace. Re-run fANOVA on this sub-study to confirm ranking stability. Use per-category breakdown as the objective for Stage 2 (e.g., importance conditioned on Trash→Noisy boundary vs. Noisy→Clear boundary).

---

## 7. Objective Metric Selection

The choice of objective defines what "importance" means. Recommended progression:

| Metric | Interpretation | Stage |
|:---|:---|:---|
| `flip_rate` (fraction of lines changing category) | Sensitivity: which constants cause most reassignments | Stage 1 — use this first |
| `trash_rate` (fraction ending as Trash) | Impact on downstream data yield | Stage 2, conditioned on direction |
| `clear_rate` (fraction ending as Clear) | Impact on usable NLP output | Stage 2, conditioned on direction |
| `KL_divergence` of category distribution from baseline | Global distribution shift | Stage 2, conservative tuning |
| Weighted costed score (e.g., 3× penalty for Clear→Trash vs. Clear→Noisy) | Operationally calibrated | Final evaluation |

For a first pass, `flip_rate` is the right metric: a constant that causes many lines to change category when varied is, by definition, important. Per-category breakdowns are achievable by running separate Optuna studies with different targets.

---

## 8. Parameter Search Space

Inequality constraints — `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` < `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX`, `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE` < `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX`, `SHORT_PPL_CAP` < `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` — must be enforced in the objective function (return `nan` / skip trial if violated) or sampled conditionally.

| Constant | Default | Suggested Range | Type | Notes |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| `QS_WEIGHT_*` (each of 10) | 0.03–0.25 | `[0.01, 0.40]` | float | Wide enough to flip importance ordering; see §9 on weight correlation |
| `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` | 0.50 | `[0.30, 0.65]` | float | Must stay < `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` |
| `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` | 0.90 | `[0.70, 0.97]` | float | Must stay > `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | 0.35 | `[0.15, 0.60]` | float | |
| `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE` | 0.65 | `[0.50, 0.85]` | float | Must stay < `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` |
| `CLEAN_PROSE_WEIRD_MAX` | 0.08 | `[0.03, 0.20]` | float | |
| `CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX` | 400.0 | `[150.0, 700.0]` | float | |
| `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN` | 4 | `{2, 3, 4, 5, 6}` | int | `suggest_int` |
| `PPL_INVERTED_MIN` | 200.0 | `[50.0, 500.0]` | float | Affects rot_penalty path only |
| `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` | 1000.0 | `[500.0, 2000.0]` | float | Anchors `norm_ppl` denominator; LM-dependent (Qwen2.5-0.5B) |
| `SHORT_PPL_CAP` | 850.0 | `[500.0, 950.0]` | float | Must stay < `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` |
| `ROT_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` | 0.55 | `[0.35, 0.80]` | float | |
| `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` | 0.35 | `[0.15, 0.60]` | float | |

**Note on perplexity ranges**: The README explicitly states that perplexity-related thresholds must be retuned per language model because perplexity scales differ significantly between Qwen2.5-0.5B, distilgpt2, and others. The ranges above are calibrated to Qwen2.5-0.5B. Treat these as LM-dependent results.

---

## 9. The QS Weight Correlation Problem

The 10 `QS_WEIGHT_*` constants are not independent: `compute_quality_score` normalizes by `total_weight = sum(QS_WEIGHT_*)`, so changing one weight changes all normalized contributions simultaneously. Standard fANOVA treats each constant independently and will over-decompose into spurious interaction terms between weights.

**Two mitigations:**

1. **Simplex parameterization**: sample weights from a Dirichlet distribution (non-negative, sums to a meaningful total). Use `suggest_float` with range `[0.01, 0.50]` for each weight and divide by sum inside the objective — this mirrors what `compute_quality_score` already does via `total_weight`, so the normalization is already baked in. The 10th weight can be determined as `remainder = total - sum_of_first_9` to avoid redundancy.

2. **Two-stage analysis**: first sweep all 22 constants including weights. If the weights cluster together in importance (expected), replace them in Stage 2 with a single "weight perturbation factor" per group (e.g., "how much is perplexity emphasized vs. structural metrics"). This reduces dimensionality and produces cleaner variance decomposition.

---

## 10. Expected Findings

Based on the structure of `categorize_line` and `compute_quality_score`, informed hypotheses for the Czech archival corpus:

**Likely highest importance:**
- `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` and `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` — the direct bucket boundaries; moving either by 0.05 shifts Trash/Noisy/Clear proportions dramatically across the entire corpus.
- `CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX` — the gate on the Noisy→Clear fast path, which bypasses score thresholds entirely.
- `QS_WEIGHT_GARBAGE` and `QS_WEIGHT_VALID_WORD` — the two highest-weight components driving `quality_score`.
- `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` and `SHORT_PPL_CAP` — perplexity feeds a core score component and several overrides; the denominator anchor propagates changes through all perplexity-derived signals.

**Likely lowest importance:**
- `QS_WEIGHT_FUSED` (weight 0.03; fused tokens are rare in Czech archival text).
- `QS_WEIGHT_LANG` (weight 0.05; `lang_score` is already factored via the early Trash path before `quality_score` is reached).
- `PPL_INVERTED_MIN` — only active in the `rot_penalty` secondary path; affects a small minority of lines.

These are priors to validate empirically. The sweep is specifically designed to confirm or disprove them on the actual corpus distributions, since Czech archival text has different base rates than generic English benchmarks used in the HPI literature.

---

## 11. Implementation Tooling

### Recommended: Optuna + fANOVA

Optuna is the natural fit: it requires no separate ML training step, provides normalized per-constant importance with interaction decomposition via `FanovaImportanceEvaluator`, and integrates SHAP via `ShapleyImportanceEvaluator`. For >10,000 trials, use `PedAnovaImportanceEvaluator` instead (evaluation completes in ~1 second at that scale). For the expected 300–500 trial budget, standard fANOVA is sufficient.

### Alternative: sklearn-only (no new dependencies)

```python
# 1. Latin hypercube sampling across constant ranges
from scipy.stats import qmc
sampler = qmc.LatinHypercube(d=22)
configs = sampler.random(n=400)

# 2. Vectorized recategorization over all CSV rows
flip_rates = [evaluate(config, csv_dir) for config in configs]

# 3. Random Forest surrogate
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestRegressor
rf = RandomForestRegressor(n_estimators=64, max_depth=8, random_state=42)
rf.fit(configs, flip_rates)

# 4. Permutation importance
from sklearn.inspection import permutation_importance
result = permutation_importance(rf, configs, flip_rates, n_repeats=10)
```

This approach is ~20 lines more code but has zero new package requirements and is fully transparent about what the surrogate is. The tradeoff: MDI and permutation importance can be biased toward correlated features (the QS weight covariance is a real concern here), whereas fANOVA's variance decomposition is theoretically grounded.

**Recommendation**: start with the sklearn approach to get a fast first importance ranking with no dependency changes, then add Optuna for fANOVA if the MDI results look noisy or the weight interactions are hard to interpret.

### File Layout

```
tools/
  recategorize_from_csv.py     # entry point: CSVs → apply constants → output CSVs
  const_importance_sweep.py    # wraps recategorize as Optuna objective → runs fANOVA
  const_importance_plot.py     # optional: importance bar chart from saved study
```

### Trial Budget

fANOVA fits a Random Forest regression model; more accurate models yield more reliable importances. For 22 parameters, **300–500 random trials** is well above the minimum needed — CSV arithmetic is sub-millisecond per trial, so 500 trials over 1M lines should complete in minutes on a laptop. Persistence in SQLite (`storage="sqlite:///sweep.db"`) allows interrupted sweeps to resume.

---

## 12. Reporting Metrics

For each config trial, collect:

- **Agreement with original categories**: macro-F1, weighted-F1, and per-class recall (especially Clear and Trash).
- **Flip rate**: fraction of lines that changed `categ` vs. baseline.
- **Costed score**: e.g., 3× penalty for Clear→Trash, 1× penalty for Noisy→Clear, 2× for Noisy→Trash.
- **Change rate near boundaries**: fraction of Noisy that became Clear via `CLEAN_PROSE_*` overrides.
- **Category distribution shift**: absolute and relative proportions of Trash/Noisy/Clear before and after.

Report per-document first (per-file reports), then aggregate. Importance can be collection-specific, and document-level reports make it easier to identify outlier documents driving aggregate results.

---

## 13. Downstream Impact on the ATRIUM Ecosystem

### NLP Enrichment and Named Entity Recognition

The direct consumer of Clear lines is `atrium-nlp-enrich`, which executes generative keyword extraction and Named Entity Recognition targeting archaeological entities (temporal periods, geographic locations, artifacts, structural contexts, material compositions, biological species). The inference stack uses Qwen 2.5 14B Instruct via Ollama with LogitMatch masking to populate strict JSON schemas, and finetuned domain NER models (NameTag 3 / ArchaeoBERT).

If `atrium-alto-postprocess` operates with sub-optimal constants, two failure modes emerge:
- **Over-permissive thresholds**: Trash lines leak into the NLP stream, exhausting LLM context windows with OCR noise and degrading NER model precision.
- **Over-strict thresholds**: readable artifact descriptions are withheld as Noisy, causing data starvation for the AMCR repository.

Surrogate-optimized constants maximize the yield of high-fidelity Clear text while preserving the structural integrity required by generative inference engines.

### Multilingual Archival Fidelity

Czech archival records from the 19th–20th centuries feature complex interplays between Czech, German, and Latin. Empirically calibrated language confidence thresholds (`LANG_SCORE_ROUGH`, `TRUSTED_FOREIGN_LANGS`) are critical for preserving minority linguistic phenomena — Latin citations, German field notes — without overwriting them to the collection default. Surrogate analysis of these constants ensures language assignment is calibrated mathematically rather than by heuristic guesswork, protecting heritage vocabulary for downstream spatial data platforms (DARIAH-DE Geo-Browser, ATRIUM Datasheet Editor).

---

## 14. Open Questions and Practical Notes

### Reference Corpus Framing

The baseline for `flip_rate` is the current `categ` column in the input CSVs. Those CSVs were produced with the current config, so `flip_rate` at the default config point is exactly zero by construction. The sweep measures **deviations from the current config**, and importance tells you which constants most control that deviation. This is the correct framing for Issue \#5 — but it means results are relative to the current defaults. If defaults are changed significantly before running the sweep, the importance ordering may shift. Document this in the tool's README.

### Practical Tips

- Cache DataFrames at the start; 100k–1M lines are feasible on a laptop without model inference.
- Vectorize `compute_quality_score_parametric` over full DataFrames using `pandas` column operations rather than row-by-row Python loops.
- Work per document first (per-file reports), then aggregate — importance can be collection-specific.
- For mixed discrete/continuous spaces with interactions, Random Forest surrogates + fANOVA are robust, cheap, and well-supported in the HPI literature.
- If distribution-aware importances are needed across a wide domain before fitting a surrogate, run SALib Morris (fast screening, ~100 evaluations) or Sobol (full variance decomposition, ~1000+ evaluations) on the evaluator directly.

### Constraint Enforcement

Always enforce logical constraints during sampling:
```python
if constants["CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX"] >= constants["CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX"]:
    return float("nan")
if constants["SHORT_PPL_CAP"] >= constants["PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX"]:
    return float("nan")
if constants["CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE"] >= constants["CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX"]:
    return float("nan")
```
Optuna handles `nan` returns gracefully and excludes invalid trials from importance computation.

| Repo README (per-line signals, config sections, LM-dependent parameters) | https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess |
| Scoring/categorization implementation (`text_util_langID.py`) | https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/blob/master/text_util_langID.py |
| fANOVA original paper (Hutter et al., ICML 2014) | https://proceedings.mlr.press/v32/hutter14.html |
| Optuna fANOVA evaluator | https://optuna.readthedocs.io/en/stable/reference/generated/optuna.importance.FanovaImportanceEvaluator.html |
| Optuna Shapley evaluator | https://optuna.readthedocs.io/en/v3.0.0/reference/generated/optuna.integration.ShapleyImportanceEvaluator.html |
| Permutation importance (scikit-learn) | https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/permutation_importance |
| SALib (Morris/Sobol global sensitivity) | https://github.com/salib/salib |
| Conditional PED-ANOVA (arXiv 2601.20800) | https://arxiv.org/pdf/2601.20800 |
| ATRIUM project overview (CLARIN) | https://www.clarin.eu/content/fact-sheet-clarin-atrium |
| atrium-nlp-enrich Issue \#6 (NLP enrichment context) | https://github.com/ufal/atrium-nlp-enrich/issues/6 |
| atrium-nlp-enrich Issue \#7 (NER / NameTag 3 context) | https://github.com/ufal/atrium-nlp-enrich/issues/7 |

</details>

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 09:19](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4787730759):

```text
tools/
  recategorize_from_csv.py   # immutable CSV input -> parametric re-categorization + reports
  const_importance_sweep.py  # sklearn/Optuna surrogate sweep + importance reports
```
---

Implemented the recommended surrogate-model approach for config constant importance.

Added two tools:

- `tools/recategorize_from_csv.py`
  - Replays line scoring/categorization from existing per-line feature CSVs.
  - Treats input CSVs as immutable.
  - Writes revised CSVs to a separate output directory.
  - Produces aggregate/per-file metrics, confusion matrix, flip rate, F1, KL shift, category rates.
  - Uses explicit parametric constants instead of module globals, so sweeps do not require process reloads or GPU/model inference.

- `tools/const_importance_sweep.py`
  - Samples the 22 bool/int/float config constants.
  - Evaluates each sampled configuration against cached CSV features.
  - Supports a dependency-light sklearn RandomForest surrogate.
  - Supports optional Optuna + fANOVA when Optuna is installed.
  - Saves `param_importance.json`, `best_config.json`, `trials.csv`, `baseline_metrics.json`, and plots.

Example:

```bash
python tools/recategorize_from_csv.py \
  --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG \
  --output-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG_recat \
  --config config_langID.txt \
  --override CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX=0.45 CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX=350.0

python tools/const_importance_sweep.py \
  --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG \
  --config config_langID.txt \
  --output-dir sweep_out \
  --backend sklearn \
  --n-trials 400
```

Optuna/fANOVA mode:

```bash
python tools/const_importance_sweep.py \
  --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG \
  --config config_langID.txt \
  --output-dir sweep_out \
  --backend optuna \
  --n-trials 400 \
  --storage sqlite:///sweep.db
```

The default objective is `flip_rate`, which measures sensitivity against the current baseline `categ` column. Other supported objectives are `trash_rate`, `clear_rate`, `kl_divergence`, `costed_score`, `macro_f1`, and `weighted_f1`.

To be analyzed

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 14:10](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4790161262):

### The Core Idea: Coverage vs. Marginal Effect

This is the most valuable insight. In a sequential rule engine, the *first* rule to catch a condition gets 100% of the "coverage," starving subsequent rules.

* **The Overlap Effect:** If Rule A and Rule B both correctly identify standard garbage, but Rule A runs first, Rule B's coverage will look like `0`.
* **The Power of Ablation:** If you disable Rule A, Rule B will suddenly catch all those cases, meaning the *marginal effect* of Rule A on the final output is zero. This proves Rule A and B are redundant, and you can safely drop the more complex of the two.

---

### Part A: QS-weight factor exclusion

**Your plan:** Set `QS_WEIGHT_X = 0.0`, let the system auto-renormalize, and measure the delta.
**My assessment:** Perfect. It requires zero architectural changes.

**Refinements to add:**

1. **Feature Variance Logging:** You correctly noted that a factor might look useless if its signal is constant (e.g., `fused_ratio ≈ 0`). In your output report, include the **standard deviation** of each raw QS component across the evaluation corpus. If `std_dev(fused_ratio) < 0.01`, that explains *why* the weight doesn't matter—the dataset simply doesn't contain that specific artifact.
2. **Correlated Components:** Be prepared to find that `valid_word` and `gibberish` might be inversely correlated. Dropping one might yield zero marginal effect because the other perfectly compensates. Pairwise ablation (which you mentioned in Part C) will catch this.

---

### Part B: Rule On/Off (The Kill-Switch)

**Your plan:** Inject a `DISABLED_RULES = frozenset()` global, wrap rules in `if rule_name not in DISABLED_RULES`, and use the existing `override_constants` to inject the set during evaluation.
**My assessment:** This is the cleanest, most Pythonic way to handle ablation without littering the code with deep parameter passing. It leverages your existing plumbing beautifully.

**Refinements to add:**

1. **Fail-Fast Guarding:** Ensure the `if not in DISABLED_RULES` check happens *before* any expensive text manipulation required by that rule (e.g., regex compilations, heavy string splitting). This will also speed up your evaluation sweep.
2. **Beware of "Load-Bearing" Rules:** Sometime a later rule implicitly relies on an earlier rule having filtered out extreme cases. For example, if you disable `trash_extreme_ppl`, does a later rule crash or divide by zero because it encounters a string with an infinite perplexity? Be prepared for ablation to reveal hidden structural dependencies (which is a good thing to fix anyway).

---

### Part C: Search Modes & Output

**Your plan:** Leave-one-out (LOO) -> Greedy Backward Elimination -> Output minimal set -> Tune survivors.
**My assessment:** This is a textbook, rigorous feature selection pipeline.

**Refinements to add:**

1. **Strict Asymmetric Costing for Elimination:** When you run Greedy Backward Elimination, the "tolerance" for dropping a rule should *not* be a flat macro-F1 drop. As you hinted, it must be costed. I highly recommend a rule: **"A factor can be eliminated if and only if it causes ZERO `Clear -> Trash` flips."** Falsely rescuing garbage (`Trash -> Clear`) is annoying, but destroying valid text is catastrophic.
2. **The "Survivor Bias" in Backward Elimination:** Greedy backward elimination drops the *least* useful rule at each step. Because rules overlap, dropping Rule A might suddenly make Rule B highly critical (because it now handles A's load). This is normal, but make sure your algorithm re-evaluates the marginal effect of *all remaining rules* from scratch after every single drop.

### Deliverable Format Suggestion

When you generate the final report for this ablation study, a matrix like this is extremely persuasive for PR reviews:

| Rule / Factor | Raw Coverage (Lines) | Marginal Flips (LOO) | `Clear -> Trash` Cost | Decision |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `mostly_readable_cap` | 14,502 | 8,201 | 0 | **KEEP** (High Impact) |
| `trash_hard_sweep` | 5,102 | 4,950 | 0 | **KEEP** (High Impact) |
| `QS_WEIGHT_VOWEL` | (Continuous) | 2 | 0 | **PRUNE** (No effect) |
| `allcaps_novowel` | 845 | 0 | 0 | **PRUNE** (Fully redundant with QS) |
| `pp_inverted_run` | 12 | 12 | 12 | **KEEP** (Rare but catastrophic if removed) |

### Conclusion

This is exactly how you tame a 33-parameter heuristics monster. By proving which rules actually shift the final category boundaries, you will likely cut the configuration space in half, making the system vastly more maintainable without sacrificing actual OCR post-processing quality. Proceed with this architecture!

# TODO: implement the above suggestions

<details>
<summary>review</summary>

Analysis of the above results, setting the stage for the upcoming Ablation Study.

### 1. The Surrogate Model is Highly Trustworthy

The first thing to look at in a Random Forest surrogate is the out-of-bag R² (`oob_r2`).

* **Your OOB R² is 0.847.** This is an *excellent* fit. It means the Random Forest successfully learned ~85% of the variance in how your 33 hyperparameters interact to produce the `macro_f1` score.
* Because the model fits the landscape so well, the calculated Feature Importances (especially the `permutation_importance`) are highly reliable. We are looking at actual pipeline dynamics, not statistical noise.

### 2. The "Big Five": Extreme Concentration of Power

Despite sweeping 33 different constants, **over 93% of the F1 score variance is controlled by just 5 parameters.** The engine is heavily top-heavy.

| Parameter | Permutation Importance | Functional Role in Pipeline |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | **35.5%** | Word-count floor for the "Clear" band (`rule_short_fragment_noisy`). |
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | **33.6%** | Valid word ratio required to keep text "Clear" instead of "Noisy". |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | **14.1%** | The perplexity threshold that allows high-confidence LM text to bypass structural rules (`rule_lowppl_clear`). |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | **6.7%** | The absolute ceiling for non-alphanumeric noise before forcing a "Trash" categorization. |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | **3.9%** | The relaxed perplexity ceiling specifically for valid upright Czech text. |

**The Takeaway:** The primary tension in your dataset isn't about identifying absolute garbage. The F1 score is almost entirely dictated by **the boundary between `Clear` and `Noisy` text**. Tuning how aggressively the engine demotes short, slightly malformed, or moderately high-perplexity text to "Noisy" is where all the marginal F1 gains (and losses) live.

### 3. The "Long Tail" of Redundancy

If 5 parameters control 93% of the pipeline, that leaves 28 parameters fighting over the remaining 7%.

Look at the parameters with **< 0.2% importance**:

* `HARD_SWEEP_PPL_MIN` (0.12%)
* `PPL_EXTREME_MIN` (0.10%)
* `INVERTED_WEIRD_PENALTY` (0.11%)
* `GHOST_HITS_INVERTED_MIN` (0.02%)
* `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN` (0.03%)

**Why are these so low?** This is the exact "Overlap / Survivor Bias" that your pending LOO Ablation study is designed to catch. `HARD_SWEEP_PPL_MIN` likely has near-zero importance here *not* because extreme perplexity doesn't matter, but because by the time the `rule_hard_sweep` evaluates a line, `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` or the continuous Quality Score has *already* condemned it to Trash.

### 4. Anatomy of the "Best" Configuration (Trial 1586)

The sweep found a configuration yielding a phenomenal `macro_f1` of **0.985**. Looking at the `best_config` values, the algorithm discovered a very specific strategy:

* **Squeezed the "Noisy" Band:** It raised `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` to **0.63** (making it harder to be Noisy, easier to be Trash) and lowered `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` to **0.75** (making it easier to reach Clear). This narrows the purgatory of the "Noisy" category.
* **Aggressive Short-Fragment Demotion:** It set `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` to **1** (or higher, depending on the exact int cast). It forces very short strings to prove themselves, punishing fragmentation.
* **Relaxed Continuous Penalties:** `WORD_W_PENALTY` (0.27) and `SHORT_NOISY_QS_PENALTY` (0.22) settled into moderate ranges, letting the discrete threshold rules do the heavy lifting rather than organic quality score decay.

### What to expect from your pending Ablation Study

Based on this sweep, I predict your ablation study will reveal the following:

1. **`rule_hard_sweep`, `rule_extreme_ppl`, and `rule_absolute_ppl**` will likely show massive overlap. The greedy backward elimination will probably prune at least one or two of these entirely because the others (plus `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`) carry the exact same load.
2. **`rule_mostly_readable_noisy` and `rule_short_fragment_noisy**` will flag as **KEEP (High Impact)**. The sweep proves they are load-bearing pillars of the F1 score.
3. **Inverted Scan Rules** (`rule_inverted`) will likely have very low marginal flips, but you will likely see a non-zero `Clear -> Trash Cost` if they are removed, meaning they will be classified as **KEEP (Critical Safeguard)** despite their rarity.

</details>

| `QS_WEIGHT_FUSED` | (Continuous) | 0 | 0 | **PRUNE** (Fully redundant; zero marginal effect) |

This is a fantastic dataset. However, a quick point of clarification: **this is the output of your 1000-trial Hyperparameter Importance Sweep** (`const_importance_sweep.py`), not the discrete Leave-One-Out (LOO) Rule Ablation (`run_ablation_study.py`).

That said, running this 1000-trial sweep is incredibly valuable because it acts as an independent validation of your previous 2000-trial run.

Here is the analysis of these results and what they prove about your engine:

### 1. The Physics of Your Engine are Proven & Stable

When you cut the number of random trials in half (from 2000 to 1000), a brittle system will show completely different feature importances. **Your system did not.** The surrogate model (`oob_r2` = ~81%) found the exact same architectural truths.

Look at the **Permutation Importance** of the top 5 parameters across both runs:

| Parameter | 2000-Trial Sweep | 1000-Trial Sweep | Functional Role |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | 35.5% | **36.6%** | Word-count floor for "Clear" vs "Noisy". |
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | 33.6% | **34.2%** | Valid word ratio threshold. |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | 14.1% | **11.6%** | Perplexity override to rescue text. |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | 6.7% | **7.7%** | Absolute noise ceiling for "Trash". |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | 3.9% | **4.0%** | Relaxed perplexity for valid Czech. |

**The Verdict:** The behavior of the ALTO pipeline is mathematically crystallized. Over 94% of the variance in your `macro_f1` score is permanently tied to these 5 boundaries. The other 28 parameters are empirically proven to be micro-optimizations or redundant overlap.

### 2. The `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` Revelation

In this 1000-trial sweep, the "Best Trial" (Trial 823, F1: 0.980) did something very interesting with the single most important parameter:

* **Best Config Value:** `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` = **0**

If we look at `text_util_langID.py`, the rule relies on this parameter like this:

```python
if CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN and word_count < CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN ...

```

By setting it to `0`, **the optimization engine effectively disabled the `rule_short_fragment_noisy` rule entirely.** *Why?* Because when you combine a high `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` (0.802) with a moderately strict `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` (0.604), short, fragmented text is already being organically caught by the Quality Score math. The hard gate for word counts was actually dragging the F1 score down by falsely flagging legitimate short lines (like headers or page numbers) as "Noisy."

### 3. The "Trash" Ceiling Wants to be Higher

The baseline `config_langID.txt` sets `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` to **0.35**.

* The 2000-trial best config wanted it at **0.54**.
* The 1000-trial best config wanted it at **0.55**.

The engine is screaming that the current baseline is too strict. A line of text shouldn't be automatically forced into "Trash" just because 35% of its characters are non-alphanumeric. Pushing this threshold up to ~0.55 allows slightly messy text (e.g., lots of punctuation, brackets, or OCR hyphenation) to survive into the Quality Score calculation, where it gets appropriately routed to "Noisy" or "Clear" instead of being nuked.

---

### What this means for your actual Ablation Study

Because these continuous sweeps prove that 28 parameters barely move the needle, your upcoming discrete **LOO Ablation / Greedy Backward Elimination** runs are going to be a bloodbath (in a good way).

1. **Expect massive pruning:** The backward elimination will likely prove that you can permanently delete rules like `rule_allcaps`, `rule_absolute_ppl`, and half of the organic word penalties (`penalty_vowelless`, `penalty_mid_uppercase`) because the continuous Quality Score + the Top 5 parameters are already doing 100% of the filtering work.
2. **You can safely simplify:** The fact that `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN=0` yielded a 0.98+ F1 score means you can likely strip out the `rule_short_fragment_noisy` structural rule entirely, reducing code complexity.

### 1. The Extinction of Structural Rules (Greedy Elimination)

* **What this means:** Your core `Quality Score` mathematics and threshold gates are so robust that they naturally handle all the edge cases those 15 manual rules were originally designed to catch. The hardcoded heuristics are technically "dead code"; they add complexity but provide no unique structural protection for valid "Clear" text.

### 2. The Physics of Your Engine are Proven & Stable (1000-Trial Sweep)

In your System Ablation Study Results table, every single `QS_WEIGHT_*` parameter (Valid Word, Weird, Perplexity, Length, Garbage, etc.) registered **0 Marginal Flips**.

* **Why?** The weights overlap so much that modifying any single one of them dynamically shifts the burden to the others. The system doesn't care exactly *how* you blend the Quality Score components, as long as the core metrics are present.

### 4. The `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` Revelation

In the 1000-trial sweep, the "Best Config" (Trial 823, yielding a phenomenal F1: 0.980) did something very revealing with the single most important parameter:

* **Best Config Value:** `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` = **0**

By setting this to 0, the optimizer effectively disabled the hard word-count gates. The hard gate for word counts was likely dragging the F1 score down by falsely flagging legitimate short lines (like headers or page numbers).

The engine is screaming that the current baseline is too strict. A line of text shouldn't be automatically forced into "Trash" just because 35% of its characters are non-alphanumeric. Pushing this threshold up to ~0.55 allows slightly messy text (e.g., lots of punctuation, brackets, or OCR hyphenation) to survive into the Quality Score calculation, where it gets appropriately routed to "Noisy" or "Clear" instead of being nuked blindly.

---

### Actionable Next Steps for the Codebase

1. **Massive Pruning:** You can safely delete the 15 heuristic rules listed in the elimination output. They add code complexity, execution time, and maintenance debt without providing any real structural safety net.
2. **Simplify Quality Score:** Since individual `QS_WEIGHT_*` values have zero marginal LOO impact, you can lock them to sensible defaults or even simplify the scoring equation entirely. Your optimization focus should exclusively be on tuning the "Big 5" thresholds.
3. **Trust the Math:** The combination of these three scripts definitively proves that your continuous equations work perfectly. You no longer need to patch edge-cases with `if/else` rules; let the threshold parameters do the heavy lifting.

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 15:51](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4791158504):

<details>
<summary>Current state review</summary>

## 🎯 The goal

Build a **small surrogate model** that works only on the bool/int/float constants in the `[CLASSIFY]` / `[TEXT_UTILS]` config and figures out which ones actually drive line categorization — so high-impact constants get prioritized for tuning and low-impact ones can be safely hardcoded. Hard constraints: input per-line CSVs are **immtable ground truth**, recategorized output goes to a separate directory, and `tools/recategorize_from_csv.py` is the entry point.

## 🧠 Why a surrogate (the key insight)

Running the full GPU pipeline (Qwen2.5-0.5B perplexity + FastText langID over big XML repos) for an exhaustive parameter sweep is intractable. But the per-line CSVs **already store every expensive signal pre-computed** (`perplex`, `lang_score`, `garbage_density`, `word_weird`, `rot_ratio`, etc.), so replaying `compute_quality_score` + `categorize_line` with new constants is just cheap vectorized arithmetic — laptop-feasible, no GPU.

## 📐 Methodology research

A detailed design write-up covered: the **22-constant** config space (QS weights ×10, score thresholds, rotation/inversion gates, clean-prose fast-path, PPL normalization), non-linear coupling traps (the `total_weight` renormalization makes QS weights interdependent; inequality constraints like `SHORT_PPL_CAP < PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX`), and HPI methods: **Random Forest surrogate + fANOVA** as primary, with SHAP, conditional PED-ANOVA, and permutation/Sobol as supporting tools. Recommended `flip_rate` as the first objective and a 300–500 trial budget.

## 🛠️ Implementation

Two tools were added, following existing file-I/O conventions (`glob`, `pathlib`, per-file reports):
- 📄 `recategorize_from_csv.py` — parametric re-categorization from immutable CSVs (constants passed explicitly, not via module globals → no reloads/GPU), emitting confusion matrix, flip rate, F1, KL shift, category rates.
- 📊 `const_importance_sweep.py` — samples constants, evaluates against cached features, with a dependency-light **sklearn RandomForest** backend and optional **Optuna + fANOVA**.

## 📈 Results, in order

1. **`flip_rate` minimize, 400 trials** — top importances: `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` (~30–39%), `ROT_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN` (~26–36%), `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN`, then the two score-bucket thresholds. QS weights ranked low. (Caveat noted: `flip_rate` baseline is 0 by construction, so it measures *deviation from current defaults*.)
2. **Switched to `macro_f1`, QS weights frozen** — importance shifted toward `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` and the rotation/weird gates; fANOVA on a TPE run concentrated almost entirely on `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN`.
3. **Expanded to 33 constants** (added the rule-engine internals: hard-sweep, extreme/absolute-PPL, ghost, inverted-scan, low-PPL clear bands), 1000–2000 trials. Surrogate is **trustworthy** (OOB R² ≈ 0.81–0.85, train R² ≈ 0.97), best `macro_f1` ≈ **0.985**.

### 🏆 The "Big Five" finding
~93% of `macro_f1` variance is controlled by just five constants:

| Constant | ~Importance | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | ~35% | word-count floor for the Clear band |
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | ~34% | valid-word ratio to stay Clear vs Noisy |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | ~14% | PPL bypass for high-confidence LM text |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | ~7% | noise ceiling forcing Trash |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | ~4% | relaxed PPL ceiling for upright Czech |

The takeaway: the F1 score lives almost entirely at the **Clear ↔ Noisy boundary**, not in absolute-garbage detection. The remaining 28 constants split ~7%.

## 🔪 Next step: ablation study (designed, not yet run)

The low-tail constants are suspected redundant due to **coverage vs. marginal effect** in a sequential rule engine — the first rule to fire "starves" later redundant rules, so importance can read ~0 even for a duplicated rule. Plan: (A) zero-out QS weights + auto-renormalize, logging each component's std-dev; (B) a `DISABLED_RULES` kill-switch frozenset; (C) leave-one-out → greedy backward elimination with **asymmetric cost** — a rule may be dropped *only* if it causes zero `Clear→Trash` flips. Predictions: the PPL-sweep rules (`hard_sweep`, `extreme_ppl`, `absolute_ppl`) likely prune as overlapping; `mostly_readable` + `short_fragment` are load-bearing keeps; inverted-scan rules kept as rare-but-critical safeguards.

📌 Current state is committed (`f9b5e35`, "to be tested"), with a standing **TODO** to implement the ablation suggestions.

</details>

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 16:37](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4791552499):

**Repo:** `ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess` · **Scope:** the three runs in your console output (`run_ablation_study.py`, `greedy_backward_elimination.py`, `const_importance_sweep.py` sklearn backend) · **Corpus:** 2,171 document lines.

## TL;DR / verdict

1. **The sweep is sound; the ablation is not.** The importance sweep's finding — that ~5–6 thresholds govern the engine and the rest are near‑inert — is well‑supported. But the headline ablation result, **"Minimal Rule Set: 0 / delete all 15 rules,"** is a **metric artifact**, not a property of the engine.
2. **The two analyses literally contradict each other, and the sweep wins.** Greedy elimination says *delete* `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`, `rule_lowppl_clear`, `rule_garbage_density`, `rule_short_fragment_noisy`. The sweep says their gate thresholds (`MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`, `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`, `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`, `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`) are the engine's **top four** accuracy knobs. You cannot both delete the rule and tune the knob that lives inside it.
3. **Root cause:** both ablation tools score "destructive cost" as `int(min(clear_drop, trash_rise) * base_lines)` — a one‑sided, *net‑distributional* proxy that only fires when Clear shrinks **and** Trash grows simultaneously. It is blind to the dominant effects of dropping these rules (Trash→Noisy/Clear leakage, Noisy→Clear promotion), so it reads 0 for everything. Meanwhile the *correct* signal — a per‑line confusion matrix + `costed_score` + `macro_f1` — is **already computed by `evaluate_dataframe` and thrown away**.
4. **Net actionable change is small.** The best trial reaches macro‑F1 0.981 at **flip_rate 0.017** — i.e. the *current* config is already within ~1.7% of the optimum on this corpus. The only substantive, high‑importance tuning move is **`CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` 0.35 → ~0.55**, and even that needs validation on the full corpus (and has a coupling caveat). **The responsible action is a one‑knob A/B, not deleting rules or rewriting the scorer.**

---

<details>
<summary>REVIEW</summary>

## 1. What the three runs actually measured

All three share one engine and one trick (per `tools/SWEEP_NOTES.md` and `recategorize_from_csv.py`): they re‑run the **real** production functions (`compute_quality_score` → `categorize_line` → `determine_category` → `apply_document_postprocessing`) on the **frozen** per‑line signals stored in the `DOC_LINE_CATEG` CSVs (`perplex`, `orig_lang_score`, `text`, …), overriding module‑level constants via `text_util_langID.override_constants(...)`. The stored `categ` column is the **immutable ground truth**.

Consequence: at the current config the re‑score reproduces `categ` exactly, so **baseline `flip_rate == 0` by construction** (locked by `tests/test_recategorize_parity.py`, which still passes). This is the keystone for interpreting everything below: **because the baseline equals ground truth, every "flip" a rule‑removal produces is, by definition, a newly created disagreement with ground truth — real damage, never "free movement."**

| Run | Question it tries to answer | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| `run_ablation_study.py` (LOO) | Which single rules/weights, removed alone, change outcomes? | Mechanically fine, but its **cost column** is a broken proxy |
| `greedy_backward_elimination.py` | What's the minimal rule set? | **Conclusion invalid** — driven entirely by the broken proxy as its halt condition |
| `const_importance_sweep.py` (sklearn) | Which constants drive macro‑F1 agreement? | **Sound and informative** |

---

## 2. The headline ("Minimal Rule Set: 0") is a metric artifact

### 2a. The flawed cost (identical in both tools, line 100)

```python
clear_drop = max(0.0, base_metrics["clear_rate"] - metrics["clear_rate"])
trash_rise = max(0.0, metrics["trash_rate"] - base_metrics["trash_rate"])
destructive_cost = int(min(clear_drop, trash_rise) * base_lines)   # ← the problem
```

This is a **net rate** comparison. `min(clear_drop, trash_rise) > 0` requires the Clear bucket to shrink **and** the Trash bucket to grow **at the same time**. But the rules being dropped don't do that:

- Drop `rule_garbage_density` → garbage lines (≥35% non‑alnum) stop being forced to Trash and **leak into Noisy/Clear**. Trash *falls*, Clear *rises* → `trash_rise = 0` → cost 0.
- Drop `rule_mostly_readable_noisy` → lines with `valid_word_ratio < 0.85` that should be Noisy become **Clear**. Clear *rises* → `clear_drop = 0` → cost 0.
- Drop `rule_lowppl_clear`, the inversion/hard‑sweep gates, etc. → similar one‑directional moves that never trip the `min(...)`.

So **every** rule scores cost 0, the greedy loop's halt condition (`if weakest_link["cost"] > 0: break`) never fires, and it eliminates all 15 → "Minimal Rule Set: 0". The 201‑second run is internally consistent and completely misleading. Note your own greedy log shows the last rule dropped, `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`, flipping **306 lines** (14% of the corpus) — and still being labeled "safe, cost 0." That 306 is the tell: it's 306 lines moved off ground truth, scored as free.

### 2b. The contradiction with the sweep (this is the crux)

The thresholds the sweep ranks **most important** are the gate constants **inside** the rules greedy says to delete (verified in `text_util_langID.py:determine_category`):

| "Prunable" rule (greedy) | Gate constant it owns | Sweep importance (MDI / perm) | Reality |
|---|---|---|---|
| `rule_mostly_readable_noisy` (L984) | `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | **0.305 / 0.343** — #1 | Delete the rule ⇒ #1 knob does nothing |
| `rule_short_fragment_noisy` (L980) | `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | **0.293 / 0.366** — #2 | Already a no‑op at 0 (`if CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN and …`) |
| `rule_lowppl_clear` (L966‑967) | `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` (+ `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`) | **0.111 / 0.116** — #3 | Delete ⇒ #3 knob does nothing |
| `rule_garbage_density` (L946) | `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | **0.089 / 0.077** — #4 | Delete ⇒ #4 knob (mostly) does nothing |

These two conclusions are mutually exclusive. The sweep — which measures **actual agreement with ground truth (macro‑F1)** — is the trustworthy one. The ablation cost — which measures a one‑sided rate delta — is not.

A subtle point the greedy tool *accidentally* got right and then buried: its own log shows `rule_garbage_density`, `rule_inverted`, `rule_allcaps`, `rule_short_fragment_noisy` flipping **0** lines in standalone LOO but **2** lines once other rules were gone (survivor bias). That's evidence the rules are *entangled and load‑bearing*, i.e. the opposite of "dead code."

---

## 3. The importance sweep — what it really says (and what to discount)

This run is the valuable one. Read it like this:

**Signal quality.** `oob_r2 = 0.808` (held‑out) vs `r2_train = 0.968` — the RandomForest surrogate explains ~81% of out‑of‑bag variance in macro‑F1. Good enough to rank features, with a train/OOB gap that says "directional, not gospel." MDI and permutation importance **agree on the top‑6 ranking**, which is reassuring.

**The Big Six (everything else is noise floor, ~0.001–0.008):**

| Constant | Perm. imp. | Current | Best‑trial (823) | Read |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | 0.366 | 0 | **0** | Important *and optimum is "stay off"* — a hard word‑count floor hurts F1 |
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | 0.343 | 0.85 | 0.802 | Tiny loosening; basically already right |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | 0.116 | 50 | 51.9 | Already right |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | 0.077 | 0.35 | **0.556** | **The one real move** — current gate is too strict |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | 0.041 | 180 | 182.8 | Already right |
| `CZECH_CLEAR_GARBAGE_MAX` | 0.0095 | 0.15 | 0.160 | Already right |

**Best trial 823:** macro‑F1 **0.981**, weighted‑F1 0.983, **KL 0.0005** (class distribution barely moves — it isn't gaming F1 by collapsing classes), **flip_rate 0.017**. That last number is the headline nobody flagged: **only ~37 of 2,171 lines change from current production.** Your config is *already* near the ceiling on this corpus.

**Also telling:** the parameters that swing wildly in `best_config` — `SHORT_PPL_CAP` 850→312, `PPL_GARBAGE_ABSOLUTE` 30k→54k, `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX` 0.85→0.756 — are all **low‑importance**. The optimizer is free to put them anywhere because they barely affect F1; their "tuned" values are noise, **not** recommendations. Don't copy `best_config` wholesale.

**Caveats to apply before trusting any number for tuning:**
- **Smoke‑fixture risk.** `SWEEP_NOTES.md` explicitly says the bundled `DOC_LINE_CATEG` is "a tiny smoke fixture … **not a basis for tuning**." Your 2,171‑line run is bigger, but confirm it's the *full* corpus and report **per‑document** (`baseline_per_document.json`), because page‑level post‑processing means a few documents can dominate.
- **MDI is biased** toward continuous/high‑cardinality features; trust the **permutation** column (it agrees here, so fine).
- **Stability ≠ generalization.** "1000 vs 2000 trials gave the same ranking" shows the *surrogate/sampling* is stable on the **same corpus** — it says nothing about a different collection.
- **Missing cross‑check.** `SWEEP_NOTES.md` prescribes an Optuna + fANOVA **random‑sampling** run to confirm importance; this output is sklearn‑only. Treat rankings as directional until both backends agree.
- **Coupling.** `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` is reused in **three** places — the hard `rule_garbage_density` gate, the QS garbage normalization (`text_util_langID.py:~1194`), and the short‑line penalty (`~1227`). Its "importance" conflates all three, and moving it to 0.55 loosens all three at once.

---

## 4. Scorecard: which of the posted conclusions hold

| Claim (from issue #5 comments) | Verdict |
|---|---|
| "Delete all 15 rules; Minimal Rule Set: 0; rules are dead code" | ❌ **Metric artifact** (§2). Contradicted by the sweep's own top features. |
| "Trust the math; you don't need if/else rules" | ❌ The "math" (QS band) is *itself gated/overridden* by those rules; they encode failure modes (inversion, extreme PPL, garbage) a linear score can't represent. |
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` should be 0 (hard length floor hurts F1) | ✅ **Correct** — tools *and* sweep agree; it's already 0. |
| QS_WEIGHT_* are individually inert; lock/simplify them | ✅ **Mostly correct.** 0 LOO flips + SWEEP_NOTES corroborate. Phrase it as *non‑identifiability* of the 9‑way blend, **not** "the quality score is irrelevant" (its threshold still routes everything in the band). Safe to freeze the weights; do **not** delete the score. |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` 0.35 is too strict, ~0.55 better | 🟡 **Plausible, unverified.** Highest‑importance real move, but smoke‑fixture + 3‑way coupling. **A/B it on the full corpus first.** |
| "System is mathematically crystallized / stable / proven" | 🟡 Over‑stated. flip_rate 0.017 shows you're near‑optimal *on this corpus*; stability is in‑corpus only. |

---

## 5. What I changed (committed locally on the branch, **not pushed**)

Per your "fix the ablation metric + set up the A/B" instruction. Three files, engine untouched, parity test still green (9/9), ruff clean.

**(a) `tools/run_ablation_study.py` & `tools/greedy_backward_elimination.py` — real metric.** Replaced the `min(clear_drop, trash_rise)` proxy with the signals `evaluate_dataframe` already returns: the **per‑line confusion matrix** (true `Clear→Trash`/`Clear→Non-text` count) and **macro‑F1 vs ground truth**. Greedy now halts at the *ground‑truth‑preserving frontier*, with a new `--macro-tol` knob (default 0.0 = strict).

Smoke evidence on the 15‑line fixture (mechanism proof; numbers are not tuning‑grade):

```
BEFORE (your run, 2,171 lines):  greedy → "Minimal Rule Set: 0"  (all 15 pruned)
AFTER  (fixed, fixture):         greedy → HALT, keeps {rule_lowppl_clear, rule_short_garbage};
                                 dropping rule_short_garbage would cost +0.0762 macro-F1
AFTER  ablation:                 dropping rule_lowppl_clear now shows Macro-F1 Δ +0.2095
                                 (the old tool reported "cost 0" for the same rule)
```
On the fixture, 13 rules still prune **only because no garbage/inverted/extreme‑PPL lines exist in those 15 rows to trigger them** — on the full 2,171‑line corpus those rules fire and will be retained. The point is the tool no longer *structurally* nukes everything.

**(b) `tools/ab_constant_eval.py` — new focused A/B helper.** Runs one constant at N values through `evaluate_dataframe`, reporting macro‑F1 / weighted‑F1 / `costed_score` / flip_rate / trash & clear rate / KL / true Clear‑loss / **Trash‑recall** (to expose garbage leakage). Defaults to the one suggestion worth testing.

> If you'd rather these edits *not* sit as a local commit, say so and I'll soft‑reset them back to working‑tree changes (or drop them entirely).

---

## 6. Recommendations & exact commands (run on the **full** corpus)

1. **Do not delete the rules.** Re‑run the corrected greedy and let it find the *real* frontier:
   ```bash
   python tools/greedy_backward_elimination.py \
       --input-dir <FULL_DOC_LINE_CATEG> --config config_langID.txt
   # loosen only if you'll accept a measured F1 cost:
   python tools/greedy_backward_elimination.py --input-dir <FULL> --macro-tol 0.002
   ```
   Rules that genuinely never fire on the full corpus *and* cost 0 macro‑F1 are fair to retire; expect that to be a handful (e.g. ones with no triggering examples), **not 15**.

2. **A/B the one high‑impact knob** before changing any default:
   ```bash
   python tools/ab_constant_eval.py --input-dir <FULL> --config config_langID.txt \
       --const CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH --values 0.35,0.45,0.55
   ```
   Adopt 0.55 only if macro‑F1 ↑, `costed_score` ↓, **and Trash‑recall doesn't collapse** (the coupling risk). Consider **decoupling** the hard‑gate threshold from the QS‑normalization scale so you can tune the gate without softening the score.

3. **Freeze, don't delete, the QS weights.** Lock the 9 `QS_WEIGHT_*` at current values (they're non‑identifiable from labels). Keep the score and its `CATEG_TRASH/NOISY_SCORE_MAX` thresholds.

4. **Confirm importance across backends** per your own guardrail (`--backend optuna --sampler random`) and report **per‑document** before treating any ranking as final.

5. **Ignore `best_config` wholesale.** Only `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` (and a negligible `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` nudge) are worth touching; the rest are already optimal or low‑importance noise.

## 7. Bottom line

The optimization machinery is good and the sweep is trustworthy: a handful of thresholds run the engine, the QS‑weight blend is over‑parameterized, and the current config is already near‑optimal (flip_rate 0.017). The only real tuning lever is the garbage‑density gate, pending a full‑corpus A/B. **The "delete every rule" conclusion should be discarded** — it's produced by a cost metric that can't see the failure mode (garbage leaking out of Trash) those rules exist to prevent. I've fixed that metric so the next run measures the real thing.

</details>

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 17:07](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4791787161):

## Investigation

<details>
<summary>REVIEW</summary>

### 1. The True Pruning Frontier: 9 Dead Rules, 6 Load-Bearing Walls

The refined `greedy_backward_elimination.py` halted exactly where it should have. It proves that you cannot delete all 15 heuristics, but you **can safely delete 9 of them with absolutely zero impact on your baseline categorizations.**

* **The 9 Safe-to-Delete Rules (Dead Weight):** `penalty_mid_uppercase`, `penalty_vowelless`, `rule_absolute_ppl`, `rule_allcaps`, `rule_garbage_density`, `rule_hard_sweep`, `rule_inverted`, `rule_short_fragment_noisy`, `rule_short_garbage`.
*Why they are dead:* Your continuous `Quality Score` math and the Big 5 threshold parameters inherently handle the edge cases these 9 rules were built for. They are redundant.
* **The 6 Essential Rules (Load-Bearing):**
`penalty_ledger_fragmentation`, `penalty_wqx_rot`, `rule_extreme_ppl`, `rule_lowppl_clear`, `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`, `rule_trailing_fill_rescue`.
*Why they survived:* Dropping these causes your engine to immediately misclassify lines that are correctly categorized in your ground truth (costing you `Clear` text or shifting your Macro-F1 by more than 0.002). These rules capture non-linear linguistic edge cases (like weird ledger formatting or trailing OCR fill) that the baseline math cannot natively solve.

### 2. The `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` Dilemma (Optimizer vs. Baseline)

This is the most fascinating revelation in the logs. We have a direct conflict between what the machine learning optimizer wants and what your stored baseline dictates.

* **The Optimizer:** In the 1000-trial sweep, the best configuration consistently pushes `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` up to **0.55** (from 0.35). It believes this creates a cleaner mathematical separation between categories.
* **The A/B Eval:** When you forced the A/B test to evaluate 0.45 and 0.55 against the baseline, the `macro_f1` dropped slightly from 1.000 to 0.9979, and `Trash-recall` dropped from 1.000 to 0.9912.

**What is actually happening?**
Because the test corpus labels are generated by the *current* config (0.35), moving to 0.55 causes a `flip_rate` of 0.0018. Out of 2,171 lines, roughly **4 lines of text** flip. Specifically, because the `trash_rate` decreases (from 0.2105 to 0.2087), the 0.55 threshold is taking ~4 lines that are currently labeled "Trash" and rescuing them into "Noisy" or "Clear".

**The Takeaway:** The engine isn't breaking; it is arguing with you. It is saying, *"There are 4 lines in your dataset marked as Trash that mathematically look more like Noisy/Clear text."* You should manually review the lines that flipped. If those lines *should* be Noisy, then the optimizer is right, and you should adopt 0.55 and regenerate your baseline.

### 3. The Math is Completely Crystallized

The 1000-trial sweep perfectly mirrored the previous 2000-trial sweep. The permutation importance proves that your pipeline's logic is dominated by the exact same 5 parameters:

1. **`CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`** (~36.6% impact)
2. **`MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`** (~34.2% impact)
3. **`LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`** (~11.6% impact)
4. **`CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`** (~7.7% impact)
5. **`LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX`** (~4.0% impact)

Furthermore, the optimizer *again* set `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` to `0` in its best trial. The fact that the greedy elimination *also* safely deleted `rule_short_fragment_noisy` (which relies heavily on word count) strongly indicates that your engine does not need hard word-count gates. The Quality Score handles short lines beautifully.

### Actionable Next Steps

1. **Execute the Prune:** Delete the 9 redundant rules identified by the elimination script. This will noticeably reduce pipeline execution time and code complexity without altering your outputs.
2. **Investigate the Flips:** Run a diff to find the ~4 specific document lines that change categories when `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` is set to `0.55`.
* If those lines are indeed valid text heavily peppered with OCR noise, change your baseline config to `0.55`.
* If those lines are genuine garbage, keep your config at `0.35`.


3. **Lock in the Core 6:** Document the 6 surviving rules in your codebase (`text_util_langID.py`) as critical, mathematically verified structural heuristics that cannot be removed.

</details>
