#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 18:05](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4792267158):

# From gpt-5

<details>
<summary>REVIEW</summary>

## Brief overall summary of Issue #5

Issue #5 started with a good practical goal: **use the already-produced per-line CSVs as immutable reference data and build a small surrogate/evaluation loop to find which `[CLASSIFY]` / `[TEXT_UTILS]` constants actually affect line categorization**. This avoids rerunning the expensive GPU/FastText/XML pipeline.

### What was implemented / discussed

The comments describe a fairly complete workflow:

- `tools/recategorize_from_csv.py`
  - Replays scoring/categorization from existing CSV features.
  - Keeps input CSVs immutable.
  - Writes recategorized CSVs separately.
  - Reports flip rate, macro/weighted F1, category rates, KL shift, confusion matrix, etc.

- `tools/const_importance_sweep.py`
  - Samples config constants.
  - Runs sklearn RandomForest surrogate, optionally Optuna/fANOVA.
  - Produces parameter importance rankings.

- Later tools / ideas:
  - `run_ablation_study.py`
  - `greedy_backward_elimination.py`
  - `ab_constant_eval.py`
  - These are used to test which rules/constants can be removed or changed.

The methodology is mostly sound: reusing precomputed `perplex`, `lang_score`, `garbage_density`, `word_weird`, `rot_ratio`, etc. is the right approach. It makes the analysis cheap and reproducible.

---

## Main result from the parameter sweeps

Across the 1000–2000 trial sklearn sweeps, the same parameters dominate. The important constants are mostly around the **Clear ↔ Noisy boundary**, not around obvious garbage detection.

The repeatedly important constants are:

| Constant | Meaning |
|---|---|
| `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` | Word-count floor / short-line handling |
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | Valid-word ratio threshold |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | Perplexity threshold for rescuing good text |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | Garbage-density cutoff |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | Czech-specific low-perplexity rescue threshold |

The comments repeatedly show that these top 5 explain most of the variance, while many other constants are near the noise floor.

### Important caveat

The current CSV `categ` values are produced by the current config, so **baseline macro-F1 is 1.0 and flip rate is 0 by construction**.

That means the sweep is excellent for answering:

> “Which constants can change the current categorization?”

But it does **not** by itself prove:

> “Which constants are objectively better for OCR quality?”

For that, you need either manual review of flipped lines or an independently labeled validation set.

---

## Ablation study: initial mistake and corrected conclusion

There was an initial conclusion that all 15 heuristic rules could be deleted, giving a “Minimal Rule Set: 0”.

That conclusion was later correctly challenged. The problem was the ablation cost metric:

```python
destructive_cost = min(clear_drop, trash_rise)
```

This missed cases like garbage leaking from `Trash` into `Noisy/Clear`, because it only detected one kind of distributional damage. So the first “delete all rules” result was a metric artifact.

After refining the metric and rerunning greedy elimination, the more credible result is:

### Safe-to-prune rules, according to the refined run

These 9 rules appeared removable on the 2,171-line sample within the chosen tolerance:

- `penalty_mid_uppercase`
- `penalty_vowelless`
- `rule_absolute_ppl`
- `rule_allcaps`
- `rule_garbage_density`
- `rule_hard_sweep`
- `rule_inverted`
- `rule_short_fragment_noisy`
- `rule_short_garbage`

### Rules to keep

These 6 survived and should currently be treated as load-bearing:

- `penalty_ledger_fragmentation`
- `penalty_wqx_rot`
- `rule_extreme_ppl`
- `rule_lowppl_clear`
- `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`
- `rule_trailing_fill_rescue`

My view: this refined 9/6 split is much more believable than “delete all rules”. But I would still not delete the 9 rules immediately without checking the full corpus and per-document reports.

---

## `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` finding

The sweeps often suggest moving:

```text
CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH: 0.35 -> around 0.54 / 0.55
```

But the direct A/B test showed:

| Value | macro-F1 vs current CSV labels | flip rate | Trash recall |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| `0.35` | `1.0000` | `0.0000` | `1.0000` |
| `0.45` | `0.9979` | `0.0018` | `0.9912` |
| `0.55` | `0.9979` | `0.0018` | `0.9912` |

So raising it to `0.55` changes only about 4 lines in the 2,171-line corpus, mostly rescuing some current `Trash` lines into `Noisy/Clear`.

My interpretation: **this is not yet evidence that 0.55 is better**. It only says the change is small and plausible. Those flipped lines should be manually reviewed. If they are readable OCR text, then `0.55` is likely better. If they are real garbage, keep `0.35`.

---

## My overall opinion

Overall, the work is going in the right direction. The surrogate/evaluation tooling is useful and the comments show a good progression: first building the sweep, then realizing the limits of naïve ablation, then refining the metric.

But I would be careful with the conclusions:

1. **The sweep is useful and credible for sensitivity analysis.**
   It identifies which constants control the current categorization behavior.

2. **It is not yet a true optimization against independent ground truth.**
   Because the “ground truth” is the current CSV categorization, any changed config is automatically penalized unless manually validated.

3. **Do not apply `best_config` wholesale.**
   Many low-importance constants move randomly in the best trials. Those values are not meaningful recommendations.

4. **Do not delete all heuristic rules.**
   The corrected result says 6 are still load-bearing. The earlier “minimal rule set = 0” should be ignored.

5. **The most actionable next step is manual review of flips.**
   Especially for `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55`.

6. **Freezing or simplifying QS weights looks reasonable.**
   Individual `QS_WEIGHT_*` constants appear hard to identify and low-impact individually. But I would freeze them, not remove the quality score machinery.

### Recommended next actions

In brief:

- Keep the surrogate tools.
- Run the refined ablation on the full corpus, not only the 2,171-line sample.
- Keep the 6 load-bearing rules for now.
- Treat the 9 prune candidates as candidates, not guaranteed deletions.
- Manually inspect the lines flipped by `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55`.
- Do not change defaults based only on surrogate “best config”.
- Add a short `SWEEP_NOTES.md` / report explaining that results are relative to current CSV labels.

</details>

Bottom line: **good engineering direction, useful tools, promising findings — but the final config/rule-pruning decisions still need full-corpus validation and manual review of changed lines.**

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-24 20:35](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4793398517):

# From Opus 4.8

<details>
<summary>REVIEW</summary>

## Review of commit 2f64341 + the full-corpus results — what holds, what to question, and where to go next

### 1. The implementation is faithful to production ✅
The three tools in `2f64341` add **no categorization logic of their own**. `run_ablation_study.py`, `greedy_backward_elimination.py` and the new `ab_constant_eval.py` all route through `evaluate_dataframe` → `recategorize_dataframe` → the real `compute_quality_score` / `categorize_line` / `determine_category` / `apply_document_postprocessing`, toggling only `DISABLED_RULES` / constants via `override_constants(...)`. One engine, not a re-implementation, and `tests/test_recategorize_parity.py` (9/9) locks `flip_rate == 0` at the current config. The corrected cost only *reads back* `confusion` / `macro_f1` / `costed_score` that `_metrics_from_labels` already produces — so the new numbers are trustworthy, and the old `min(clear_drop, trash_rise)` → "Minimal Rule Set: 0" was confirmed to be a metric artifact.

Nuance worth stating: greedy's `macro_drop` is measured against the **frozen `categ`** (cumulative), i.e. it scores *deviation from the current config* — exactly the "preserve categories" goal, but **not** "correctness" (see §3).

### 2. "Delete the 9 dead rules" — not yet, and not all 9
The 9/6 split is real but narrower than it reads:
- Only **4** rules are *truly inert* on this corpus (Flips 0, Macro-F1 Δ +0.0000): `rule_inverted`, `rule_garbage_density`, `rule_short_fragment_noisy`, `rule_allcaps`.
- The other **5** are pruned only because they fit under `--macro-tol 0.002` — they **do** move ground-truth labels: `penalty_vowelless` (+0.0004), `rule_absolute_ppl` (+0.0005), `penalty_mid_uppercase` (+0.0006), `rule_hard_sweep` (+0.0012), `rule_short_garbage` (+0.0019). At `--macro-tol 0` only the 4 inert ones drop.
- "Inert" here = *no triggering examples in these 19 documents*. `rule_inverted` / `rule_allcaps` / `rule_garbage_density` / `rule_hard_sweep` guard rotated scans, all-caps scramble, garbage and extreme-PPL lines — failure modes that may simply be absent in this corpus and present in the next collection. They are O(1) guards; deleting them trades microseconds for a lost safety net on data we haven't measured.

**Suggestion:** read the result as *"redundant on DOC_LINE_CATEG (19 docs, tol 0.002)"*, not *"dead code."* Keep the cheap structural guards; retire a rule only with coverage evidence across multiple collections.

### 3. The factor review is a map of *leverage*, not a tuning prescription
This is the part I'd most question. `macro_f1` is scored against a ground truth that **the current config generated** (`flip_rate == 0` by construction), so the objective is **maximized at the current config** — the optimizer can never beat 1.0, and `best_config` is the *closest deviation*, not an improvement. Therefore:
- "Importance" = **sensitivity** (which knob most changes the output), not direction or goodness. `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` at ~36% with optimum `0` means *"don't raise this"* — and it's already 0. `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` and `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` land essentially at current → no action.
- The one move the sweep keeps suggesting, `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` 0.35→0.55, your own A/B then **falsifies**: macro-F1 1.000→0.9979, **Trash-recall 1.000→0.9912** (~4 Trash lines leak into Noisy/Clear). And that A/B isn't even a clean test of the gate: `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` is reused in `determine_category` at the hard gate (L946) **and inside the quality score** (garbage normalization L1191/L1194, short penalty L1227, trailing-fill L891). Raising it loosens the gate *and* inflates the score for garbagey lines simultaneously, so the 4 flips conflate both effects.

Honest read: **none of these self-referential runs justify changing a single threshold.** Their value is showing us *where the model is sensitive* — i.e. where labeling and decoupling will pay off.

### 4. Alternative approaches to the parameter-choice problem
What would let us *improve* rather than only *preserve*:

1. **Break the self-reference with a small config-independent gold set.** Hand-label a few hundred lines decided by a human, not by the current config. Only then can the sweep/A-B find configs that *beat* today's, and the garbage A/B becomes a real test. Let the tools pick *what* to label: the A/B flip set + the highest-variance lines across sweep trials = an active-learning / disagreement pool, so each label buys maximum information.
2. **Decouple reused constants.** Split `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` into a hard-gate threshold vs a QS-normalization scale (audit other constants shared across QS + gates). Then importance is attributable and the gate is tunable without moving the score.
3. **Proper variance decomposition for importance.** RF-MDI is biased toward continuous/high-cardinality params (per our own `SWEEP_NOTES`); prefer Sobol/fANOVA with Sobol/LHS quasi-random sampling, cross-check backends, and **report per-document** — 19 docs with page-level post-processing means a few documents can dominate the global number.
4. **Optimize the operational cost, not raw agreement.** We already compute `costed_score` (Clear→Trash = 3.0, …). Optimizing that, or `macro_f1` *subject to* a Trash-recall floor, bakes in "garbage must not leak" — the exact failure mode the old proxy was blind to.
5. *(Longer term)* once a gold set exists, consider replacing the hand-tuned threshold stack with a small **monotonic, interpretable model** (monotonic GBM / calibrated logistic): same transparency, no threshold treadmill.

### 5. Concrete, safe next steps
Keep all 15 rules; change no defaults. (a) Diff and eyeball the ~4 `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55` flips to seed a gold set; (b) prototype the gate/QS decoupling; (c) re-run importance with Sobol sampling + per-document output. **Re-tune only against gold labels.**




# Add a Sobol (variance-based) sensitivity backend to the constant sweep (issue #5)

## Context
Parameter "importance" today comes from a RandomForest **surrogate** (MDI + permutation,
`oob_r2≈0.81`) and Optuna **fANOVA**. Both are surrogate-fit estimates and RF-MDI is biased
toward continuous / high-cardinality features (it distorts the integer gates
`CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`, `GHOST_HITS_INVERTED_MIN`, `INVERTED_RUN_MIN`). `SWEEP_NOTES.md` already
flags that importance needs (quasi-)uniform sampling. A **Sobol** variance decomposition adds
what the current methods can't give cleanly:

- **Model-free**: indices are computed on the *real* engine outputs — no surrogate error.
- **First-order `S1` vs total-order `ST`**: `ST − S1` quantifies each parameter's involvement in
  **interactions**, and `S2` names which *pairs* interact. This would have flagged the
  `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` gate↔score coupling automatically (expect `ST ≫ S1`).
- **Unbiased / equal footing** across float and integer params; `S1` reads as "fraction of
  output variance explained."

**Honest limit (must keep stating):** the objective `macro_f1` is scored against the
self-generated ground truth (maximized at the current config by construction). Sobol gives
cleaner *sensitivity/interaction* attribution but still **cannot recommend better thresholds** —
real tuning needs config-independent gold labels. Sobol is a better *importance/coupling* tool,
not an optimizer.

## The blocking constraint (drives the design)
`validate_constants` (`tools/recategorize_from_csv.py:529`) imposes **cross-parameter**
inequalities: `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX < CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX`,
`CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE < CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX`, `SHORT_PPL_CAP < PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX`.
The RF backend copes by **rejection sampling** (`run_sklearn_backend` retries until valid).
Sobol/Saltelli sampling is a **structured matrix** (A, B, ABᵢ) — you cannot reject/resample
rows without destroying the estimator, and `analyze` cannot take NaN. Inputs must also be
~independent over a box.

**Resolution (v1):** restrict the Sobol study to the **constraint-free** parameters. The
constrained members are exactly the *low-importance* ones
(`CATEG_TRASH/NOISY_SCORE_MAX`, `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE`, `SHORT_PPL_CAP`,
`PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX`); every high-importance knob (`MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`,
`CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`, `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`, `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`, `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX`)
is unconstrained — so this loses nothing that matters. (Future work: reparameterize constrained
pairs as `gap`/`fraction` variables to recover a fully-valid box for all-param Sobol.)

## Approach
Two-stage, reusing the existing harness end-to-end:
1. **Morris screening** (cheap, `r·(D+1)` evals) to rank the 33 params by `mu_star` and spot
   nonlinearity/interaction via `sigma`.
2. **Sobol** (`N·(2D+2)` evals) on the screened constraint-free survivors (≈6–10 params) for
   `S1`/`ST`/`S2` with confidence intervals.

Use **SALib** (`ProblemSpec`: `sample_sobol`/`analyze_sobol`, `sample_morris`/`analyze_morris`) —
mature, pure-Python, `evaluate(func, nprocs=…)` for parallelism. `scipy` is already present but
only gives the sequence, not the estimators, so SALib is the right dep.

## Needed changes

### 1. `tools/const_importance_sweep.py` (main work — mirror the existing backends)
- `--backend` choices (`L536`): add `"sobol"` and `"morris"`.
- New args: `--sobol-N` (base sample, default 128), `--no-second-order`, `--nprocs` (parallel
  eval), `--morris-r` (trajectories, default 20).
- `run_sobol_backend(...)` and `run_morris_backend(...)`, parallel to `run_sklearn_backend`
  (`L303`) and `run_optuna_backend` (`L407`). Each:
  - Build the SALib `problem` from `SEARCH_SPACE` (`L93`) for the active `params` (names +
    `[low,high]` bounds). **Guard:** if any active param is in a constrained group, drop it with
    a warning (or require `--allow-constrained`); document the reparam path.
  - Sample → for each row build `constants = {**base_constants, **dict(zip(params,row))}`, round
    `INT_CONSTANTS`, `coerce_constants` (`recategorize_from_csv.py:516`), then
    `evaluate_dataframe(data, constants, **eval_kwargs)` (`recategorize_from_csv.py:708`) and pull
    the metric via `objective_value` (`L242`). Wrap as the `func(X)->y` SALib expects.
  - Analyze → return a result dict in the **same shape** as today (so JSON/CSV/plot reuse):
    `sobol_S1`, `sobol_ST`, `sobol_S1_conf`, `sobol_ST_conf`, `sobol_S2` (and `morris_mu_star`,
    `morris_sigma`); reuse `normalize_importances` (`L249`) for an `ST`-based ranking.
  - Reuse `save_json` (`L270`), `write_trials_csv` (`L274`), `save_importance_plot` (`L278`,
    plot `ST`), and `maybe_sample_documents` (`L257`) to shrink per-eval cost if needed.
- Dispatch in `main()` (`L615`) on the new backends.
- Update the top-of-file methodology docstring (`L23-28`) to add Sobol/Morris: model-free,
  interaction-aware, needs the structured sample, restricted to constraint-free params.

### 2. `tools/requirements-sweep.txt`
- Add `SALib>=1.4` (note: optional, sweep-only, like optuna/matplotlib).

### 3. `tools/SWEEP_NOTES.md`
- Document the new backends: when to prefer Sobol (unbiased + interactions + model-free), the
  Morris→Sobol two-stage, the constraint restriction, and the cost guidance below.

### 4. (Optional) `tests/`
- A tiny smoke test: run `--backend sobol --sobol-N 4` on the fixture over 2–3 unconstrained
  params; assert `S1`/`ST` keys exist and lengths match. Mirror any existing sweep test.

## Cost guidance (≈1.5 s/eval on 2,171 lines, measured from the greedy run)
- Morris screen, D=33, r=20 → ~680 evals ≈ **18 min**.
- Sobol, screened D=8, N=256 (2nd-order) → 8·256·… ≈ 4,608 evals ≈ **~2 h**; N=128 ≈ **~1 h**.
- Full D=33, N=128 → 8,704 evals ≈ **~3.6 h** (use `--nprocs` and/or `--sample-docs`).
Recommend Morris→Sobol on the survivors; run on the cluster (container has only the 19-doc
fixture, so numbers here are smoke-only).

## Verification
1. Add SALib; `python -m pytest -q` unaffected (new backend is additive).
2. Smoke (machinery only, 15-line fixture):
   `python tools/const_importance_sweep.py --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG --config config_langID.txt --backend sobol --sobol-N 8 --top-param MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN,LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX,CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`
   → emits `S1`/`ST`/`S2`; assert `ST ≥ S1` per param.
3. Morris smoke: same with `--backend morris --morris-r 4` → emits `mu_star`/`sigma`.
4. On full corpus (user, cluster): expect Sobol top-rank to broadly match permutation importance
   (`MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`, `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`, `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`,
   `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`) and `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` to show `ST > S1` (coupling).
5. `ruff check` / `ruff format --check` on changed files.
Deliver results in chat; commit locally on `claude/pensive-maxwell-1xwe9t`, **do not push**.

## Out of scope / paused
- Full-space Sobol over the constrained params (needs the gap/fraction reparam) — future work.
- No default value changes; no rule deletion.
- **Paused but approved:** the `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` gate/score decoupling
  (`QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX`). When it lands it auto-joins the study as a 34th tunable; Sobol on the
  two garbage knobs would then separate gate vs score sensitivity directly.




# Decouple `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`: hard gate vs. quality-score scale (issue #5)

## Context
The importance sweep flags `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` as a high-leverage knob and its
joint optimum sits near 0.55, but the isolated A/B (`0.35 -> 0.55`) on the full 2,171-line
corpus *loses* agreement and leaks garbage (macro-F1 1.000 -> 0.9979, Trash-recall
1.000 -> 0.9912). Root cause: the constant is used for **two different jobs** at once —
a hard categorization gate AND an internal quality-score scale — so the A/B can never
test the gate cleanly, and the sweep's "importance" for it conflates both mechanisms.

This change splits the constant into two independently tunable knobs, **behavior-preserving
by default** (both default to 0.35, so the engine's output and the `flip_rate == 0` parity
baseline are unchanged). After this, the gate threshold can be A/B'd / swept without
touching how the score normalizes garbage, and importance becomes attributable.

Decided with the user: implement the decoupling; chat-only delivery, **no push**.

## The split (verified usage sites in `text_util_langID.py`)
Keep `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` for the **categorization gate**:
- L891 `_trailing_fill_rescued` (the gate's rescue escape hatch)
- L946 `determine_category` hard Trash gate (`garbage_density >= …`)

Move to a **new `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX`** (the quality-score garbage scale) — the three
`compute_quality_score` sites only:
- L1191 short-clean half-weight check (`garbage_density < max(…, 1e-9)`)
- L1194 garbage normalization denominator (`norm_garbage = 1 - min(garbage/ max(…), 1)`)
- L1227 short-line penalty trigger (`garbage_density >= …`)

(No other module uses the constant — `langID_classify.py` etc. are clean.)

## Changes

### 1. `text_util_langID.py`
- After L115, add: `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX = _get_float("TEXT_UTILS", "QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX", 0.35)`
  (mirrors the `QS_LENGTH_MAX` / `PERPLEXITY_THRESHOLD_MAX` "QS scale" family).
- Replace `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` -> `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX` at **L1191, L1194, L1227 only**.
- Leave L891, L946 unchanged.

### 2. `config_langID.txt`
- Under `[TEXT_UTILS]`, next to `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.35`, add `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX=0.35`
  with a one-line comment ("quality-score garbage scale; decoupled from the hard gate").

### 3. `tools/recategorize_from_csv.py`
- Add `"QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX"` to `_THRESHOLD_NAMES` (L394-433, beside `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`
  at L397). This auto-registers it in `TUNABLE_CONSTANTS` (L434), `DEFAULT_CONSTANTS`
  (`_live_default` reads the new live attr), `read_config_constants` validation, `coerce_constants`,
  and `override_constants`. It's a float, so **no** `INT_CONSTANTS` change.

### 4. `tools/const_importance_sweep.py`
- Add to `SEARCH_SPACE` (L99-area): `"QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX": {"type": "float", "low": 0.15, "high": 0.60}`
  — **required**, the L139-141 guard raises if any tunable lacks a range.
- Add `"QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX"` to `THRESHOLD_PARAMS` (L163-177); it is auto-included in the
  `default`/`full` profiles via `DEFAULT_SWEEP_PARAMS`. (EDGE_PARAMS optional — leave out.)

## Behavior preservation / parity
Both constants default to 0.35 and the config sets both to 0.35, so `compute_quality_score`
is numerically identical and every category is unchanged. `tests/test_recategorize_parity.py`
must stay 9/9 (`flip_rate == 0`). If any test hardcodes the tunable count (was "33 params"),
update it to 34.

## Verification
1. `python -m pytest tests/test_recategorize_parity.py -q` -> 9/9 (defaults unchanged).
2. `python -m pytest -q` (full suite) — catch any hardcoded-count assertions; fix if needed.
3. Clean **gate-only** test (the original goal):
   `python tools/ab_constant_eval.py --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG --config config_langID.txt --const CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH --values 0.35,0.55`
   — now moves only the hard gate; compare its Trash-recall delta to the old coupled run.
4. **Score-only** test: same command with `--const QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX`.
5. `python tools/const_importance_sweep.py --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG --config config_langID.txt --output-dir /tmp/sweep_out --backend sklearn --metric macro_f1 --n-trials 50`
   — confirm it sweeps **34** params and reports the two garbage knobs separately.
6. `ruff check` / `ruff format --check` on changed files.
Report results in chat; commit locally on `claude/pensive-maxwell-1xwe9t`, **do not push**.

## Out of scope
- No change to the default 0.35 for either knob (tuning waits on gold labels).
- No rule deletions. No other constant decoupling yet (garbage only, as agreed).
- Full-corpus A/B + sweep are the user's to run on the cluster (container has only the
  19-doc smoke fixture); commands provided.



# Gold-label / active-learning seed from the A/B + boundary lines (issue #5, alt #1)

## Context
Every importance/A-B/sweep number so far is scored against the **self-generated** `categ`
(`flip_rate == 0` at the current config by construction), so the objective is **maximized at
today's config** — it can rank leverage and catch regressions, but it can never say a *different*
config is genuinely **better**, and it falsely "punished" the `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` 0.55
move. The only fix is a ground truth **independent of the current config** = a small set of human
labels. To spend labeling effort well, label exactly the lines the parameters are most uncertain
about: the A/B flip set + decision-margin + rule-boundary lines (active learning).

This plan delivers (1) a tool that extracts a prioritized **label queue**, and (2) a small,
**correct** gold-scoring path so that — once those lines are labeled — the existing A/B and sweep
can target human truth and a config can finally exceed the current one (and the 0.35-vs-0.55
garbage question gets an empirical answer).

## Piece 1 — `tools/build_label_queue.py` (active-learning extractor; main work)
Score every line for informativeness, then write `label_queue.csv` for humans.

Signals (union; each line keeps why + a score):
1. **A/B flips** — for each constant in a probe set (default: high-importance, constraint-free
   knobs + candidate grids: `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH {0.45,0.55}`,
   `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN {0.80,0.90}`, `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX {40,60}`,
   `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX {160,200}`), `recategorize_dataframe` and diff vs baseline per line;
   record `n_flips` and the set of categories the line takes (`alt_categories`).
2. **Decision margin** — lines whose recomputed `quality_score` is within ε (≈0.05) of a band
   boundary (`CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX`, `CATEG_NOISY_SCORE_MAX`).
3. **Rule-boundary** — lines decided by the kept load-bearing rules, via the stored reason flags
   (`lowppl_clear`, `trash_threshold`, `noisy_threshold`, `cleanprose_clear`).
4. *(optional)* **Sweep sensitivity** — union flips of a few sampled configs / the sweep
   `best_config`.

Mechanics: `load_csvs` → baseline `recategorize_dataframe` (== stored `categ` by parity) → per
probe config `recategorize_dataframe` + per-line diff joined on `(file, page_num, line_num)` →
aggregate. Output columns: locators, `text`, `categ` (clearly labeled *suggestion, not truth*),
`quality_score`, `perplex`, `garbage_density`, `word_count`, reason flags, `why_selected`,
`n_flips`, `alt_categories`, `margin`, an **empty `gold_categ`** (allowed: Empty/Non-text/Trash/
Noisy/Clear) and `notes`. Sort by `n_flips` desc then `margin` asc; spread with `--per-doc-cap`
and cap with `--max-lines` (default ~250); optional stratify by `categ`. Reuses
`recategorize_dataframe` (recategorize_from_csv.py:304), `_coerce_locators` (:275),
`read_config_constants` (:473), `_load_lang_config` (:122); thresholds from the live constants.
No engine change.

## Piece 2 — correct gold scoring (small; makes the labels usable)
Page-level post-processing needs whole pages, so we **must recategorize the full corpus but score
only the labeled rows** — not filter the input. Add an optional `gold_column` to
`evaluate_dataframe` (recategorize_from_csv.py:708): predict over the full df as today, then
restrict `_metrics_from_labels` to rows whose `gold_column` value is non-empty (set `original` from
that column). Everything downstream (`confusion`, `macro_f1`, `costed_score`) is reused unchanged.
Then add a `--gold-col` (+ `--label-file` to merge `gold_categ` back onto the corpus by locators)
passthrough to `tools/ab_constant_eval.py` and `tools/const_importance_sweep.py`. Note: vs gold the
baseline `flip_rate` is no longer 0 (that is the whole point) — soften the sweep's
"expect flip_rate≈0" log when `--gold-col` is set.

## Needed changes
- **New** `tools/build_label_queue.py` (Piece 1).
- `tools/recategorize_from_csv.py`: add `gold_column` param to `evaluate_dataframe` (recategorize
  full, score labeled subset).
- `tools/ab_constant_eval.py` and `tools/const_importance_sweep.py`: add `--gold-col` /
  `--label-file` → pass `gold_column` into `evaluate_dataframe`.
- `tools/SWEEP_NOTES.md`: document the queue → label → gold-score loop and that gold scoring is the
  only way the objective can exceed the current config.
- *(optional)* `tests/`: smoke test that `build_label_queue` emits a non-empty queue with the
  expected columns incl. empty `gold_categ`; and that `evaluate_dataframe(gold_column=...)` scores
  only labeled rows.

## Verification
1. Smoke (15-line fixture): `python tools/build_label_queue.py --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG --config config_langID.txt --max-lines 20`
   → writes `label_queue.csv` (locators+text+empty `gold_categ`+`why_selected`/`n_flips`/`margin`);
   the `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` boundary line(s) appear.
2. Hand-label a few rows, then
   `python tools/ab_constant_eval.py --input-dir data_samples/DOC_LINE_CATEG --config config_langID.txt --const CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH --values 0.35,0.55 --gold-col gold_categ --label-file label_queue.csv`
   → metrics computed vs gold on the labeled subset (baseline ≠ 1.0).
3. `python -m pytest -q` unaffected (parity test still uses the default `categ`); `ruff` clean.
4. Full corpus (user, cluster): build a ~200-line queue, label the garbage-boundary lines, and
   settle 0.35-vs-0.55 against human truth; optionally `const_importance_sweep --gold-col` for a
   first *real* tuning pass.

## Out of scope / sequencing
- Running the full gold-tuned sweep is downstream of collecting labels.
- **Paused but approved (independent):** the `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` gate/score decoupling
  (`QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX`) and the Sobol/Morris backend. This gold workflow is what makes both
  *evaluable against truth* once labels exist.

</details>

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-25 05:03](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4796048632):

https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/commit/b4bd545937e196209714be443d3f99c37aec0073 - current state

**Core Refactoring: Parameterizing Page Context & Pruning Dead Rules**

* **Retired Legacy Constants & Rules:** * Completely removed the `rule_short_fragment_noisy` hard-gate rule and its associated configuration variable `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`.
* Removed legacy "near-boundary promotion" constants (`CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE`, `CLEAN_PROSE_WEIRD_MAX`, `CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX`, `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN`).


* **Config-Driven Page Context Smoothers:** * Replaced hardcoded float literals (e.g., `0.15`, `0.60`, `0.80`) in the `apply_document_postprocessing` function with configurable constants (e.g., `SURROUNDED_TRASH_QS_MARGIN`, `PAGE_CLEAN_CLEAR_MIN`, `PAGE_GARBAGE_NOISY_QS_MAX`).
* Added these new constants to `config_langID.txt` so they can be overridden and evaluated.


* **Tooling & Sweep Updates:** * Updated `const_importance_sweep.py` and `recategorize_from_csv.py` to remove the deprecated `CLEAN_PROSE` and `CLEAR_BAND` variables from the search space and parameter lists.
* Injected the new page-context thresholds into the tuning scripts so the optimizer can sweep them.


* **Test Suite Adjustments:** * Removed `TestClearBandGuard` tests in `test_categorization_routes.py`.
* Added `TestLowPplFastTrack` to explicitly test that high-confidence, low-perplexity text correctly bypasses the retired word-count gates and gets promoted to `Clear`.

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-25 05:49](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4796277458):

### **The Problem Context (Issue #5)**

The goal of Issue #5 is to optimize the hyperparameters and heuristic rules of the ALTO XML OCR post-processing pipeline. The current system assigns categories to OCR lines (e.g., `Clear`, `Trash`, `Noisy`) using a highly complex web of thresholds and rules. The team suspects the system suffers from **"Survivor Bias,"** meaning many overlapping rules are redundant because they mask each other's utility.

The tools run experiments against a frozen "ground-truth" dataset to see which parameters actually matter and which rules can be safely deleted without moving lines into the wrong categories.

---

### **1. Random Forest Parameter Importance Sweep**

**The Output:** `[sklearn] completed 1000/1000 valid trials...`

* **What it did:** The script generated 1,000 random configurations across 36 different pipeline hyperparameters. It then trained a Random Forest surrogate model (`oob_r2: 0.809`) to calculate which parameters most heavily dictate the `macro_f1` score.
* **Interpretation:** The pipeline is heavily over-parameterized. Out of 36 tunable constants, just **four** do roughly ~84% of the heavy lifting for the entire system:
1. `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` (~45.5% importance)
2. `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` (~21.1% importance)
3. `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` (~12.2% importance)
4. `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` (~5.6% importance)

* **Takeaway:** Dozens of constants (like `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX`, `HARD_SWEEP_PPL_MIN`, and `PPL_INVERTED_MIN`) have less than 1% importance. They are essentially noise, confirming that the categorization logic can be drastically simplified.

### **2. Greedy Backward Elimination (Strict & Relaxed)**

**The Output:** `Starting Greedy Backward Elimination...`

* **What it did:** The algorithm iteratively disabled the least impactful heuristic rule out of 14 total rules, checking the "real damage" to the ground-truth categories at each step.
* **Interpretation of the Strict Run (`macro-tol = 0.0`):** * Three rules (`rule_garbage_density`, `rule_allcaps`, `rule_inverted`) were dropped with exactly **0 flips** and **0 impact** on macro-F1. This proves they are 100% redundant on this dataset and their filtering load is already handled by other rules.
* **Interpretation of the Relaxed Run (`macro-tol = 0.002`):**
* By allowing a microscopic 0.2% drop in the macro-F1 score, the script safely pruned **8 out of 14 rules**.
* Even after deleting more than half the rules, only 9 lines (out of 2,171) changed categories. Furthermore, the `Clear-loss` was exactly 0, meaning not a single line of good text was accidentally demoted to `Trash` or `Non-text`.

* **Takeaway:** You can safely reduce the pipeline down to a minimal set of just **6 rules** (`penalty_ledger_fragmentation`, `penalty_wqx_rot`, `rule_extreme_ppl`, `rule_lowppl_clear`, `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`, `rule_trailing_fill_rescue`).

### **3. A/B Constant Evaluation**

**The Output:** `A/B on CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH over 2,171 lines...`

* **What it did:** The script tested the sweep's main actionable recommendation: relaxing the `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` threshold from its aggressive baseline of `0.35` up to `0.45` and `0.55`.
* **Interpretation:** * Pushing the value up to `0.55` caused almost no disruption. The `macro_f1` only dropped by `-0.0021`.
* `Trash-recall` remained at 99.12%, meaning less than 1% of garbage text managed to "leak" into higher-quality categories. `Clear-loss` remained at 0.

* **Takeaway:** It is entirely safe to apply the `0.55` value to production. The system is robust to this threshold shift, confirming the hypothesis from the importance sweep.

### **Conclusion**

The logs successfully validate the suspicions raised in Issue #5. The current OCR classification pipeline is highly redundant and over-engineered. By stripping away the 8 overlapping rules identified by the elimination script and focusing tuning efforts solely on the top 4 parameters identified by the Random Forest, you can vastly simplify the codebase without degrading its ground-truth accuracy.

#### <img src="https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/65828620?u=80b39d3cb2967c52e1d4af28dcefc7a1efdfdc79&v=4" width="50">[K4TEL](https://github.com/K4TEL) commented at [2026-06-25 06:13](https://github.com/ufal/atrium-alto-postprocess/issues/5#issuecomment-4796401531):

# By GPT 5.5

<details>
<summary>Updated brief report on the new Issue #5 state</summary>

I reviewed the newer issue content. The direction is still good, but the newest comments mix **valid findings** with a few conclusions that are too strong.

The issue has evolved from “build a surrogate to rank constants” into a broader calibration/refactoring effort:

- surrogate sweeps over config constants,
- ablation / greedy rule elimination,
- A/B checks for high-impact constants,
- proposed Sobol/Morris sensitivity backend,
- proposed gold-label / active-learning queue,
- recent refactor `b4bd545` removing some legacy constants/rules and adding tunable page-context thresholds.

---

## What changed since the previous summary

### 1. Commit `b4bd545` refactored the rule/config surface

According to the comment on page 71–72, the current branch now:

- removed `rule_short_fragment_noisy`,
- removed `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN`,
- removed legacy `CLEAN_PROSE_*` constants:
  - `CLEAN_PROSE_MIN_SCORE`
  - `CLEAN_PROSE_WEIRD_MAX`
  - `CLEAN_PROSE_PPL_MAX`
  - `CLEAN_PROSE_WC_MIN`
- parameterized page-context smoothing constants in `apply_document_postprocessing`, e.g.:
  - `SURROUNDED_TRASH_QS_MARGIN`
  - `PAGE_CLEAN_CLEAR_MIN`
  - `PAGE_GARBAGE_NOISY_QS_MAX`
  - `PAGE_CLEAN_MEDIAN_QS_MIN`
  - etc.
- updated the sweep tooling to use the new parameter list.
- added tests around the low-PPL fast-track behavior.

This is a meaningful change: the sweep now has **36 parameters**, not the older 33.

---

## Latest sweep result

The newest 1000-trial sklearn sweep, shown on pages 72–75, reports:

```text
r2_train ≈ 0.968
oob_r2   ≈ 0.809
n_params = 36
```

That is similar to previous results: the Random Forest surrogate is fitting the parameter-response landscape reasonably well. It is good enough for **sensitivity ranking**, though not enough to treat exact percentages as universal truths.

### New top parameters

The latest permutation importance ranking is dominated by:

| Constant | Permutation importance | Interpretation |
|---|---:|---|
| `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` | ~0.528 | dominant Clear/Noisy threshold |
| `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` | ~0.238 | low-perplexity Clear rescue |
| `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` | ~0.128 | garbage threshold |
| `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` | ~0.051 | Czech-specific low-PPL rescue |
| `CATEG_TRASH_SCORE_MAX` | ~0.0067 | much lower now |
| most page-context constants | ~0.001–0.002 | low impact in this corpus |

This is consistent with the earlier story: **the engine is mostly controlled by a few Clear/Noisy rescue/readability gates**, not by most of the long-tail thresholds.

The previous `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` used to appear highly important, but it has now been removed. After removal, its importance seems to have shifted into `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` and `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`, which makes sense.

---

## Latest greedy elimination result

After the refactor, the greedy tool evaluates **14 rules**.

### Strict mode, `--macro-tol 0`

The strict run on page 76 says only 3 rules can be dropped with exactly zero impact:

- `rule_garbage_density`
- `rule_inverted`
- `rule_allcaps`

Remaining required rules: 11.

This is a much more conservative and believable result than the earlier “delete everything” conclusion.

### Relaxed mode, `--macro-tol 0.002`

The relaxed run on page 77 prunes 8 rules:

- `penalty_mid_uppercase`
- `penalty_vowelless`
- `rule_absolute_ppl`
- `rule_allcaps`
- `rule_garbage_density`
- `rule_hard_sweep`
- `rule_inverted`
- `rule_short_garbage`

It keeps 6:

- `penalty_ledger_fragmentation`
- `penalty_wqx_rot`
- `rule_extreme_ppl`
- `rule_lowppl_clear`
- `rule_mostly_readable_noisy`
- `rule_trailing_fill_rescue`

This matches the earlier refined 6-rule core, except `rule_short_fragment_noisy` has already been removed.

### My interpretation

I would phrase this carefully:

- **Strictly zero-impact on this 2,171-line / 19-document corpus:** only 3 rules.
- **Low-impact within tolerance 0.002:** 8 rules.
- **Still load-bearing:** 6 rules.

I would not call all 8 “safe to delete in production” yet. Some are probably absent because this corpus does not contain their failure modes. `rule_inverted`, `rule_allcaps`, and `rule_garbage_density` are cheap structural guards; removing them may be fine for this sample but risky on broader OCR data.

---

## A/B result for `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`

The newest A/B result is unchanged:

| Value | macro-F1 vs current labels | flip rate | Trash recall | Clear loss |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `0.35` | `1.0000` | `0.0000` | `1.0000` | `0` |
| `0.45` | `0.9979` | `0.0018` | `0.9912` | `0` |
| `0.55` | `0.9979` | `0.0018` | `0.9912` | `0` |

This means raising the threshold from `0.35` to `0.55` changes around 4 lines, mostly current `Trash` lines being rescued into higher categories.

### Important correction

The newest comment on page 79 says:

> “It is entirely safe to apply the 0.55 value to production.”

I disagree with that wording.

A/B shows that `0.55` causes **small disruption**, not that it is objectively better. Since the labels are generated by the current config, the A/B is still self-referential. The correct conclusion is:

> `0.55` is a plausible candidate worth manual review because it only flips a few lines and causes no Clear-loss, but it should not be adopted until those flipped Trash lines are inspected or validated against gold labels.

If those 4 lines are readable text incorrectly marked as Trash, then `0.55` is better. If they are real garbage, keep `0.35`.

---

## About the newest “over-parameterized” conclusion

The newest comment says the pipeline is highly over-parameterized and can be drastically simplified. Broadly, yes — the sweep repeatedly shows a small number of parameters dominate.

But I would separate three claims:

### Supported

- The parameter space is over-large.
- Most constants have very low observed importance on this corpus.
- The main leverage sits in:
  - `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN`
  - `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX`
  - `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`
  - `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX`

### Partially supported

- Some rules are redundant on the 2,171-line corpus.
- `rule_short_fragment_noisy` / `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` removal looks reasonable if parity/tests pass.

### Not yet supported

- “Apply `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55` to production.”
- “Delete all low-impact rules globally.”
- “The optimizer found better defaults.”

The current objective is still measured against the current config’s generated labels. That makes the sweep a sensitivity study, not true optimization.

---

## Good new proposals in the issue

The new issue contains several good future directions.

### 1. Sobol / Morris backend

The proposal on pages 63–66 is strong.

Why it helps:

- model-free sensitivity, no RandomForest surrogate bias,
- separates first-order `S1` from total-order `ST`,
- can expose interactions such as `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` being coupled to multiple mechanisms.

Caveat: Sobol still measures sensitivity against the current labels unless gold labels are added. So it improves importance attribution, not correctness.

### 2. Decouple `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH`

The proposal on pages 67–69 is also strong.

Current problem:

`CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` apparently affects both:

- hard Trash gate,
- quality-score garbage normalization / penalties.

That means changing it changes multiple things at once.

The proposed split:

- keep `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` for the hard gate,
- add `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX` for quality-score scaling.

This is the right engineering move. It preserves current behavior if both default to `0.35`, while allowing cleaner A/B tests later.

### 3. Gold-label / active-learning queue

The proposal on pages 69–71 is probably the most important.

The current setup can tell us:

> “What changes current labels?”

It cannot tell us:

> “What is actually better?”

The proposed `build_label_queue.py` would generate a focused human-labeling set from:

- A/B flips,
- boundary lines,
- rule-triggered lines,
- high-disagreement lines.

That is exactly the right way to turn this from self-referential calibration into actual model improvement.

---

## My current recommendation

### Keep

Keep the surrogate tooling:

- `recategorize_from_csv.py`
- `const_importance_sweep.py`
- `ab_constant_eval.py`
- corrected greedy / ablation tooling

These are useful.

### Treat as validated / mostly OK

- Removing `CLEAR_BAND_WC_MIN` / `rule_short_fragment_noisy` appears reasonable if tests and parity pass.
- Removing `CLEAN_PROSE_*` legacy constants may be fine if low-PPL fast-track tests cover the intended behavior.
- Parameterizing page-context constants is good.

### Do not yet do

- Do not blindly apply the full `best_config`.
- Do not treat `0.55` for `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` as production-ready.
- Do not delete cheap safety rules globally based only on this 19-document corpus.
- Do not claim the system is “optimized”; it is currently “sensitivity-mapped.”

### Next best actions

1. **Manually inspect the ~4 lines flipped by `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55`.**
2. **Implement or finish the gold-label queue.**
3. **Decouple `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` from `QS_GARBAGE_NORM_MAX`.**
4. **Run the same sweeps against gold labels once available.**
5. **Only then decide whether to change defaults.**
6. **Keep the 6 load-bearing rules.**
7. **For the 8 relaxed-prune rules, classify them as “candidate prune / corpus-redundant”, not “dead”.**

</details>

---

## Bottom line

The new results strengthen the earlier conclusion that the pipeline is **over-parameterized** and dominated by a few readability / low-perplexity / garbage thresholds.

However, the latest conclusion that `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH=0.55` is “safe for production” is too strong. The A/B result only shows a small deviation from current labels, not correctness. The right path is now clear: **decouple the garbage threshold, build a small gold-label set from the flip/boundary cases, and retune against human truth.**

In short: **good progress, better tooling, cleaner refactor — but final config changes and rule deletions still need gold-label or broader-corpus validation.**
