# By Gemini DR Pro 3.1

<details>
<summary>
Architectural and Operational Analysis of the ATRIUM ALTO XML Post-Processing Pipeline: Optimizing Heuristic Categorization via Surrogate Modeling
</summary>

### **Overview of the ATRIUM Post-Processing Framework and Cultural Heritage Digitization**

The large-scale digitization of historical and archival documents represents a formidable challenge within computational linguistics and digital humanities. At the center of this challenge is the inherent instability of Optical Character Recognition (OCR) systems when confronted with degraded physical media. Raw OCR output, which is frequently encoded in the ALTO (Analyzed Layout and Text Object) XML standard, inherently suffers from a multitude of structural and linguistic anomalies. These anomalies stem from physical document degradation, typographical inconsistencies typical of historical printing presses, erratic margin structures, archival stamps, and complex multi-column layouts that confuse traditional sequential parsing algorithms. To systematically address these profound data quality issues, the Institute of Formal and Applied Linguistics (ÚFAL) at the Faculty of Mathematics and Physics, Charles University in Prague, has spearheaded the development of the atrium-alto-postprocess pipeline.1
This highly sophisticated, multi-stage processing architecture is specifically designed to ingest raw ALTO XML files, extract semantic text sequences, evaluate the linguistic and structural quality of those sequences, and systematically filter out irrecoverable noise.2 The post-processing framework does not operate in isolation; rather, it functions as a critical foundational layer within the broader ATRIUM research infrastructure.3 The ATRIUM project constitutes a comprehensive ecosystem aimed at the enrichment, semantic mapping, and translation of XML-based cultural heritage data.1 By transforming raw, geometrically defined bounding boxes and raw XML trees into cohesive, logically ordered textual streams accompanied by robust probabilistic confidence metrics, the atrium-alto-postprocess pipeline ensures that subsequent downstream systems are supplied with high-fidelity, structurally sound inputs.2
The intricacies of this post-processing pipeline present significant operational challenges, specifically regarding the computational overhead required to process large terabyte-scale historical archives. This comprehensive report provides an exhaustive assessment of the current state of the post-processing framework. It rigorously analyzes the system's structural extraction methodologies, its highly optimized asynchronous computational architecture, and the advanced algorithmic techniques employed for text quality categorization. Furthermore, this analysis conducts a deep dive into an active engineering bottleneck—extensively documented in the repository's Issue \#5—concerning the severe computational friction of hyperparameter tuning in hardware-asymmetric environments. The report meticulously evaluates the proposed surrogate modeling strategy designed by the research development team to overcome these limitations, while contextualizing these optimization efforts within the broader hardware constraints of the ATRIUM Work Package 4 (WP4) and Work Package 5 (WP5) deliverables.4

### **The ATRIUM Ecosystem and Inter-Repository Dependencies**

To fully comprehend the design constraints imposed upon the atrium-alto-postprocess architecture, it is necessary to examine its position within the macroscopic ATRIUM operational ecosystem. The Institute of Formal and Applied Linguistics maintains several heavily interconnected repositories that manage the lifecycle of the digitized data from raw ingestion to final semantic knowledge extraction.1 The ALTO XML post-processor operates upstream of critical natural language processing modules, most notably the atrium-nlp-enrich repository and the atrium-translator repository.1
The atrium-translator system is tasked with the in-place translation of complex XML files (including both ALTO and AMCR standards) into the English language, thereby standardizing localized European archival data for global accessibility.1 If the upstream post-processor fails to accurately classify and reconstruct the logical reading order of a document, the machine translation algorithms will be fed fractured morphemes and structurally incoherent sentences, resulting in catastrophic translation failures. Similarly, the atrium-nlp-enrich framework relies on the sanitized output of the post-processor to execute complex Named Entity Recognition (NER), keyword extraction, and structural semantic mapping.3
The administrative and developmental trajectory of these interconnected systems is formally governed by ATRIUM's Work Package 4 and Work Package 5\.5 Work Package 5 is explicitly dedicated to "Knowledge representation and processing technologies," making the high-quality textual output of the OCR categorization pipeline the fundamental raw material required for the fulfillment of the entire work package's objectives.5 Furthermore, the integration of the post-processing pipeline into external institutional frameworks is actively tracked via comprehensive integration issues, such as the ARUP-CAS/aiscr-webamcr Issue \#3530, which explicitly monitors the deployment of the atrium-alto-postprocess tool within the Fedora repository ecosystem.7 This web of dependencies mandates an exceptionally low tolerance for false positives (preserving garbage text) within the post-processor, as any noise that escapes the categorization phase will invariably pollute the downstream knowledge representation databases.

## **Tri-Modal ALTO XML Text Extraction Methodologies**

The primary and most computationally complex challenge of ALTO XML processing lies in the transition from a purely spatial, coordinate-based representation of characters to a logically coherent, one-dimensional text stream. Historical documents exhibit extreme structural variance. They range from structurally straightforward, single-column modern prints to severely degraded, multi-column medieval or early modern manuscripts featuring complex marginalia, erratic line spacing, and pervasive end-of-line hyphenation.4 To accommodate this vast structural diversity without universally defaulting to computationally prohibitive, hardware-saturating methods, the atrium-alto-postprocess architecture implements an advanced tri-modal extraction strategy.2 This strategy dynamically applies different extraction protocols based on the specific topological complexity of the ingested document.
These extraction methodologies are encapsulated within distinct Python execution scripts—specifically extract\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py, extract\_LytRdr\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py, and extract\_LLM\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py.2 Each script is rigorously optimized for a specific architectural trade-off between raw processing speed (throughput) and spatial reconstruction fidelity (accuracy).

| Extraction Protocol | Execution Script | Computational Bounding | Core Methodological Capability | Target Document Typology |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **alto-tools (Direct Parsing)** | extract\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py | CPU-bound / Low Memory | Direct traversal and string extraction from the XML Document Object Model (DOM). | Linear, structurally simple layouts lacking complex multi-column interactions. |
| **LayoutReader (Spatial Reconstruction)** | extract\_LytRdr\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py | CPU-bound / Moderate Compute | Reconstructs logical reading order by calculating vectors between spatial bounding boxes. | Standard complex documents, multi-column texts, documents with heavy hyphenation. |
| **GLM-4v-9b (Visual Language Model)** | extract\_LLM\_ALTO\_2\_TXT.py | GPU-bound / Extremely High Compute | Replaces heuristic parsing with deep visual-spatial inference using raw document pixels and geometric hints. | Severely degraded historical texts, irregular margins, texts heavily obscured by archival stamps. |

### **The CPU-Bound Direct Parsing Protocol**

For archival documents identified as structurally simplistic—such as modern typewritten pages featuring linear layouts, single columns, and minimal spatial fragmentation—the pipeline utilizes the alto-tools method.2 This protocol relies on a heavily optimized, strictly CPU-bound parsing framework derived from the widely utilized cneud/alto-tools repository, which the pipeline's setup sequence explicitly clones and installs.2
The direct parsing protocol bypasses complex spatial reconstruction algorithms entirely. Instead, it relies on high-speed iteration directly over the underlying XML element tree. By adopting the operating assumption that the structural hierarchy encoded by the original OCR engine (e.g., the nested sequence of \<TextBlock\>, \<TextLine\>, and \<String\> tags) perfectly correlates with the logical human reading order, this method achieves exceptionally high data throughput. However, its fundamental reliance on the raw XML hierarchy renders it highly vulnerable to layout misinterpretations. Legacy OCR engines frequently fracture multi-column texts horizontally across the physical page rather than correctly grouping them vertically down the distinct columns. Consequently, the alto-tools method is utilized strictly within highly controlled parameters, reserved exclusively for environments where document layouts are guaranteed to be linear or where computational resources are so severely restricted that more advanced methods are mathematically unviable.

#### **The Spatial Reconstruction Protocol**

To circumvent the inherent limitations of direct DOM parsing, the primary extraction mechanism deployed by the ATRIUM pipeline is the LayoutReader method.2 Operating at a moderate, yet highly parallelizable computational cost, LayoutReader conducts deep mathematical analyses of the explicit spatial bounding boxes (HPOS, VPOS, WIDTH, HEIGHT) embedded within the ALTO XML format to computationally reconstruct the logical reading order independently of the OCR engine's XML hierarchy.4
A critical operational advantage of the LayoutReader protocol is its advanced handling of intra-word morphological breaks. Historical documents frequently utilize aggressive end-of-line hyphenation to force block justification. A naive DOM parser treats these split textual components as completely separate lexical entities, which severely degrades downstream linguistic analysis, disrupts Named Entity Recognition, and causes artificial, cascading spikes in neural model perplexity.4 LayoutReader actively detects the spatial coordinates and typographic indicators of hyphenation across physical line breaks. It seamlessly fuses these fractured, hyphenated segments back into single contiguous string tokens before the data is permitted to pass into the linguistic evaluation stage.4 To accomplish this, the pipeline's setup process requires the precise integration of a specialized v3 layout framework imported from the external LayoutReader repository, establishing a highly effective balance between deep analytical spatial reasoning and CPU-bound throughput.2

#### **The Visual Language Model Fallback Protocol**

For the most challenging and chaotic edge cases—which are frequently characterized by severely degraded historical typography, erratic or non-existent margins, massive archival stamp overlays that occlude text, and deeply irregular historical layouts—deterministic geometric heuristics ultimately fail. In these scenarios, the pipeline dynamically falls back to a highly intensive Visual Language Model (VLM) approach.2 This method is driven by the GLM protocol, utilizing a patched version of the massive GLM-4v-9b visual-language architecture, executing entirely within the rigid bounds of available GPU memory.4
This protocol abandons traditional XML node parsing and coordinate geometry almost entirely. Instead, it ingests the raw pixel data of the digitized document overlayed with the sparse geometric hints from the ALTO files. By applying self-attention mechanisms over the visual tokens, the model visually infers text flow, effectively simulating human visual interpretation of complex spatial structures.4 Due to the immense GPU memory footprint (VRAM) and the substantial inference latency associated with operating a 9-billion parameter multimodal network, this protocol represents a significant bottleneck and is utilized strictly as an automated last resort. The deployment of GLM-4v-9b in this highly specific context indicates a profound and sophisticated awareness within the ATRIUM engineering team that deterministic, rule-based heuristics are mathematically insufficient for recovering data from the highest tiers of cultural heritage document corruption.

### **Asynchronous Asymmetric Computational Architecture**

Following the complex spatial extraction phase, the pipeline is immediately tasked with determining the linguistic validity and the physical layout quality of the resulting reconstructed text lines. To accomplish this, the system must evaluate individual strings across multiple structural, statistical, and neural dimensions. Because some required metrics (such as calculating vowel ratios) demand computationally trivial arithmetic while others (such as calculating linguistic coherence) demand deep neural network inference, processing these lines in a simple sequential loop would result in catastrophic hardware bottlenecks, characterized by massive GPU idle times while the system waits for the CPU to parse text.4
To optimize throughput and ensure maximum hardware saturation, the architectural design of the atrium-alto-postprocess pipeline (specifically Workflow Stage 4.1) implements a highly advanced, asymmetric CPU/GPU processing concurrency model.2 The system explicitly bifurcates processing tasks based on their specific computational profiles—CPU-bound versus GPU-bound—utilizing a shared asynchronous polling queue to manage highly efficient inter-process communication.

#### **CPU Pre-Filtering and High-Speed Heuristic Processing**

The architecture allocates a substantial pool of up to 32 independent CPU worker threads to aggressively manage operations categorized as low-latency, strictly deterministic, or memory-bound.4 These workers handle the initial File I/O operations, loading the reconstructed, post-LayoutReader text lines directly into system memory.
Crucially, before any line of text is permitted to enter the asynchronous queue for advanced, GPU-bound neural evaluation, it must pass through a mandatory CPU Pre-filter.2 This pre-filtering stage applies high-speed deterministic checks to immediately flag lines that require no further computational expenditure. For instance, the system executes an instantaneous structural check via the pre\_filter\_line() function to assign an Empty category to any string array consisting entirely of whitespace characters or null tokens.2 This immediate algorithmic culling is paramount; it prevents the highly valuable GPU queue from being saturated with non-informative, geometrically blank data.
Simultaneously, the 32 CPU workers are responsible for executing the language identification module.4 Utilizing the highly efficient FastText architecture, specifically the lid.176.bin model distributed by Facebook and HuggingFace, the CPU calculates a rapid vector-based language confidence score for every extracted line.2 FastText's reliance on subword n-gram feature hashing makes it exceptionally fast and highly resilient to the minor character transpositions and localized spelling corruptions that are ubiquitous in OCR output. Concurrently, the CPU threads compute a comprehensive suite of structural detection heuristics—evaluating alphanumeric ratios, capitalization densities, and symbol distributions—before formatting this consolidated statistical matrix into a data packet and pushing it into the shared asynchronous loop that feeds the GPU.2

#### **Dedicated GPU-Bound Linguistic Evaluation**

Operating as an isolated singleton within the concurrent pipeline, a dedicated GPU worker exclusively hosts the generative language model responsible for advanced linguistic evaluation.4 Specifically, the system utilizes the Qwen2.5-0.5B architecture, though it explicitly supports alternative models such as distilgpt2 for corpora known to be strictly English.2 The deliberate engineering choice to limit the GPU worker to a highly compressed 0.5-billion parameter model prioritizes rapid inference velocity and high batch-throughput over deep semantic comprehension, which is reserved for downstream pipelines.2
The sole responsibility of the GPU worker is to continually ingest the text lines pulled from the asynchronous queue and calculate a highly specific mathematical metric: the linguistic perplexity score.2 Perplexity serves as a profoundly powerful indicator of structural text coherence. In the mathematical context of autoregressive language modeling, perplexity ![][image1] for a sequence of tokens ![][image2] is defined as the exponentiated average negative log-likelihood of a sequence. Because Qwen2.5-0.5B is pre-trained on vast, normalized corpora of well-formed human text, it assigns high probability values to standard syntactic and morphological constructions, while assigning precipitously low probabilities to sequences resembling OCR noise (e.g., fractured morphemes, random symbol injections, failed ligatures). Consequently, noisy, corrupted OCR lines yield exponentially high perplexity scores.
By isolating this calculation-heavy tensor operation strictly to the dedicated GPU worker, the architecture guarantees that the neural inference does not stall the parallel File I/O, FastText evaluations, and structural heuristic algorithms executing simultaneously across the 32 CPU threads.4

### **Multi-Signal Feature Engineering and Composite Scoring**

The central objective of the quality classification stage is to mathematically assign each extracted line of text a definitive quality category.2 This critical decision is never derived from a single metric, as isolated heuristics are highly prone to edge-case failures. Instead, the pipeline synthesizes multiple distinct signals evaluated during the asymmetric processing phase into a comprehensive, multi-dimensional matrix.
The system relies on a rigorous ten-signal composite framework to generate a final, unified metric, internally designated as the quality\_score, which is strictly bounded within the normalized mathematical range of ![][image3].2 This composite value functions as a probabilistic confidence indicator representing the text's ultimate utility for downstream NLP enrichment. The computation relies heavily on a set of pre-calculated, per-line features that are maintained in structured data arrays and eventually logged directly into output CSV files for permanent archival paradata storage.4

#### **Core Feature Definitions and Linguistic Mechanics**

The individual signals utilized to compute the final quality\_score are rigorously designed to detect highly specific failure modes inherent to algorithmic spatial text extraction. The primary features include:

| Feature Variable | Computational Origin | Analytical Purpose and Typological Indication |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **perplex** | GPU (Qwen2.5-0.5B / distilgpt2) | Measures linguistic fragmentation. High values indicate poorly merged bounding boxes, unrecognized fonts, or absolute algorithmic failure by the OCR engine resulting in random character substitution.2 |
| **lang\_score** | CPU (FastText lid.176.bin) | The confidence threshold representing morphological adherence to any of the 176 supported human languages. Low confidence strongly implies catastrophic character-level corruption that transcends simple spelling errors.2 |
| **garbage\_density** | CPU (Structural Heuristic) | Quantifies the spatial prevalence of non-standard symbols relative to total line length. High densities of unexpected glyphs (e.g., \#, @, |, \~) appearing outside mathematical contexts typically pinpoint scanner noise, dust artifacts, or archival stamps erroneously read as text.4 |
| **word\_weird** | CPU (Structural Heuristic) | Evaluates adherence to expected lexical geometries. Words lacking vowels entirely, or containing impossible consonant clusters in the identified baseline language, mathematically elevate this penalty score.4 |
| **vowel\_ratio** | CPU (Character-level Metric) | Assesses the proportion of phonetic vowels to total alphabetic characters. Texts falling significantly outside standard linguistic boundaries (e.g., 30-45% for typical Indo-European languages) are probabilistically flagged as potential digital noise.4 |
| **rot\_ratio** | CPU (Spatial/Geometric Metric) | Indicates potential catastrophic issues with physical document orientation. Inverted scans, sideways inserts, or skewed pages often produce localized pockets of text that algorithmically resemble random character streams, which this precise metric seeks to isolate.4 |
| **caps\_header** | CPU (Boolean Deterministic Flag) | Evaluates typographical capitalization logic. If all alphabetic words within a line are fully capitalized, this flag triggers. While indicative of valid section headers, when mathematically combined with high garbage\_density, it frequently identifies misinterpreted physical document borders or framing lines.2 |

These distinct vectors undergo a sequence of mathematical normalizations and are fed directly into the compute\_quality\_score function, which leverages these weighted parameters to output the unified ![][image3] confidence index, setting the stage for discrete categorical assignment.2

### **Categorization Logic and Post-Processing Contextual Smoothing**

Upon the successful mathematical computation of the continuous quality\_score, the pipeline executes its core categorization logic via the categorize\_line function.2 This critical module maps the continuous confidence interval into highly discrete operational categories. This classification represents the final arbiter of truth, strictly determining the fate of the extracted text in all subsequent knowledge representation and natural language translation stages.

#### **The Five-Tier Classification Schema**

The post-processing system maps every evaluated line to one of five distinct categorical states based on a complex cascade of nested heuristic rules, threshold gates, and absolute hard boundary overrides.4 The operational definitions of these categories are as follows:

| Classification Category | Downstream Fate | Defining Characteristics and Heuristic Triggers |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Clear** | Preserved | The highest quality tier. The textual line passes all structural heuristics, maintains a dominant lang\_score, exhibits minimal perplex, and possesses a high composite quality\_score. Passed directly to ATRIUM enrichment pipelines without alteration.4 |
| **Noisy** | Preserved / Flagged | Characterized by moderate structural degradation. Exhibits minor anomalies such as fused tokens (missing whitespace), irregular capitalization logic, or mild perplexity spikes. Preserved but explicitly flagged for automated downstream correction prior to knowledge base integration.4 |
| **Trash** | Discarded | Indicates severe, irrecoverable text corruption. Triggers when the score falls below strict quality thresholds or when hard override rules are violated (e.g., massive rot\_ratio violations indicating inverted scans, or unrecoverable all-caps gibberish). Completely expunged from the active dataset.4 |
| **Non-text** | Filtered | Designed for technically accurate OCR that lacks semantic value. Captures lines that are mathematically too short, possess too few unique symbols, fall below a 30% threshold for alphabetic characters, or perfectly match known structural archival codes (e.g., library call numbers). Filtered to prevent Named Entity Recognition confusion.4 |
| **Empty** | Ignored | Assigned instantaneously and exclusively to whitespace-only or null lines detected during the initial, high-speed CPU pre-filter phase, preventing them from consuming further computational resources.2 |

#### **Contextual Smoothing and Macroscopic Aggregation**

Algorithmic classification evaluated purely at the isolated, micro-level line is inherently prone to minor contextual aberrations. For example, a perfectly pristine, highly coherent string of text embedded deep within a massively degraded, water-damaged paragraph might technically achieve a high quality\_score in isolation; however, contextually, it is highly likely to be part of a broader structural failure, making its semantic isolation misleading.
To systematically mitigate this statistical vulnerability, the pipeline applies a robust "Post-Processing Smoothing" algorithm (formally designated as Workflow Stage 4.1).2 This mechanism probabilistically evaluates the categorical assignments of neighboring spatial lines. If an isolated Clear line is bounded geometrically by multiple Trash or Non-text lines, the smoothing algorithm dynamically downgrades the Clear line, assuming that the regional degradation renders the isolated text semantically unreliable.
Following this smoothing phase, the pipeline enters the Memory Bound Aggregate Statistics phase (Workflow Stage 4.2).2 Here, the micro-level per-line classifications are mathematically aggregated into macroscopic document-level statistics. These vital metrics are compiled into standardized tables—such as the arup\_page\_stats\_SHORT.csv document—utilizing the dedicated atrium\_paradata.py module for comprehensive paradata logging.2 The production of these detailed statistical readouts is critical, as it allows project curators to assess the viability and digital health of massive, multi-terabyte archival ingests at a glance, without requiring manual textual review.

### **The Optimization Bottleneck: Parameterization and Computational Intractability**

Despite the profound architectural sophistication of the extraction and categorization phases, a critical, system-threatening engineering challenge arises regarding the calibration of the mathematical thresholds that govern the categorization logic itself. The atrium-alto-postprocess configuration relies fundamentally on a vast array of constants—specifically boolean toggles, integers, and floating-point values—defined precisely within configuration blocks such as and.4
These configuration constants dictate the exact mathematical boundaries where a line transitions from Clear to Noisy, or is abruptly discarded as Trash. For instance, altering the maximum permissible vowel\_ratio by a fraction of a percent, or marginally lowering the acceptable boundary for the final quality\_score, can drastically alter the final textual output of the entire pipeline, potentially deleting millions of valid words or allowing vast quantities of OCR garbage to flood the downstream translators. In standard machine learning operations, the conventional approach to fine-tuning such parameters is an exhaustive hyperparameter sweep: systematically altering the constants in tiny increments, running the entire dataset through the complete model, and continuously measuring the resulting variance in output accuracy to find the mathematical optimum.
However, as exhaustively detailed in the project's GitHub Issue \#5 by the system's lead research developer (@K4TEL), executing iterative parameter sweeps over the existing post-processing pipeline is mathematically, logistically, and temporally intractable.4 The fundamental bottleneck is the asymmetric processing architecture itself. Rerunning the full GPU pipeline—which necessitates repeatedly loading massive ALTO XML files into memory, engaging the computationally expensive LayoutReader spatial reconstruction, running the FastText structural analysis on 32 concurrent CPU threads, and recalculating neural perplexity via the Qwen2.5-0.5B tensor operations—requires an immense, unjustifiable expenditure of compute time and electrical energy.4
An exhaustive, grid-search style parameter sweep testing thousands of micro-variations in the \`\` constants over terabytes of archival data would paralyze the available GPU infrastructure for weeks or months. This physical reality makes iterative sensitivity analysis completely impossible on standard hardware or developer laptops, severely hindering the project's ability to adapt the pipeline to new, highly idiosyncratic historical corpora.4

## **Surrogate Modeling for High-Velocity Configuration Sensitivity Analysis**

To resolve the computational deadlock outlined in Issue \#5, the ATRIUM development team conceptualized and engineered a powerful architectural circumvention: the implementation of a lightweight, highly vectorized surrogate modeling loop explicitly designed to calculate parameter importance without ever invoking the heavy neural infrastructure or the spatial parsers.4
The fundamental algorithmic realization enabling this elegant approach is that the computationally expensive operations—specifically the XML coordinate geometry parsing, the VLM visual inference, the FastText n-gram processing, and the LLM perplexity generation—are entirely deterministic with respect to a given text line. A specific line of OCR text will always yield the exact same perplex and lang\_score regardless of how the \`\` thresholds are configured. The tunable thresholds only dictate the final discrete categorization step, not the underlying continuous feature values.

#### **The Immutable CSV Data Strategy**

The surrogate pipeline framework relies on treating the output of a single, full-scale, highly expensive GPU run as an absolute, inviolable "ground truth" reference dataset.4 During this initial, one-time pipeline execution, the system exports highly detailed per-line CSV files that contain every pre-computed, computationally expensive feature (including perplex, lang\_score, garbage\_density, word\_weird, vowel\_ratio, and rot\_ratio) alongside its original categorical assignment.4
For the precise purposes of the surrogate model, this input directory of CSVs is treated as strictly immutable.4 This paradigm shift successfully severs the lightweight categorization logic from the incredibly heavy neural extraction phase entirely.

#### **The recategorize\_from\_csv.py Implementation Workflow**

The execution of this surrogate logic is managed via a newly proposed, highly specialized development tool: tools/recategorize\_from\_csv.py.4 This script is engineered to run locally on a standard developer laptop CPU, bypassing high-performance computing clusters entirely. It achieves this by utilizing basic, highly optimized vectorized arithmetic via data science libraries like Pandas or NumPy.
The operational workflow of the surrogate script proceeds through several highly optimized stages:

1. **Ingestion:** It rapidly loads the immutable, pre-computed per-line CSVs directly into volatile memory (RAM).
2. **Configuration Injection:** It accepts a modified, experimental configuration file containing speculative tweaks to the bool, int, or float constants.
3. **Vectorized Re-Categorization (Replay):** By passing the pre-computed features through the compute\_quality\_score and categorize\_line functions using the newly injected constants, it rapidly assigns new categories to millions of text lines in mere seconds, entirely bypassing the GPU, the ALTO XML parsing trees, and the FastText neural calls.4
4. **Memory Optimization:** The architecture strongly emphasizes vectorization over the CSV features. Vectorized operations execute arithmetic across entire data arrays simultaneously, effectively preventing the out-of-memory (OOM) errors and processing bottlenecks that would inevitably arise from iterating through the massive data structures sequentially, line by line.4
5. **Output Isolation:** The resulting re-categorized outputs are written to a strictly separate output directory, permanently preserving the integrity and immutability of the baseline ground truth data.4

#### **Strategic Goal of the Sensitivity Analysis**

The overarching engineering objective of this surrogate evaluation loop is to perform a high-velocity parameter sensitivity analysis. By rapidly sweeping through potential constant values and recalculating the outputs in seconds, the tool can mathematically identify which specific configuration parameters possess high variance impact. A high variance impact indicates that minor numerical tweaks to a constant drastically alter the resulting categorizations.4
Parameters mathematically identified as highly impactful to the quality\_score will be explicitly isolated for careful, manual, expert-driven tuning. Conversely, constants identified as having low or negligible impact on the final categories can be safely hardcoded into the pipeline's source code, dramatically reducing systemic configuration complexity and streamlining all future archival deployments.4

### **Evaluation Metrics for Configuration Impact and Shift Detection**

Evaluating the true efficacy of a parameter change requires deeply rigorous mathematical tracking. It is wholly insufficient to merely state that a parameter altered the output; the exact nature, magnitude, topological direction, and statistical significance of that shift must be precisely quantified. To facilitate this rigorous evaluation, the recategorize\_from\_csv.py tool is meticulously designed to generate a comprehensive suite of comparative statistical metrics between the baseline (ground truth) categorizations and the experimental surrogate outputs.4

#### **Volatility and Structural Mapping Metrics**

The system reports on several high-level indicators of systemic change, providing immediate feedback on configuration volatility:

| Evaluation Metric | Technical Definition | Analytical Purpose in Parameter Tuning |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Flip Rate** | A direct percentage metric representing the total volume of text lines that underwent any category reassignment (e.g., moving from Clear to Noisy) under the new configuration.4 | A high flip rate instantly flags a parameter as highly sensitive and potentially volatile, demanding careful manual review. |
| **Category Rates** | The absolute distribution of the five defined categories (Clear, Noisy, Trash, Non-text, Empty) across the entire evaluated dataset.4 | Identifies if a parameter tweak causes catastrophic unbalancing, such as a threshold error that suddenly reclassifies 80% of a valid document as Trash. |
| **Confusion Matrix** | A standard ![][image4] tabular layout comparing the predicted classifications of the experimental configuration against the actual classifications of the immutable baseline.4 | Allows developers to observe highly specific misclassification pathways, revealing, for example, if an experimental tweak to vowel\_ratio disproportionately flags Clear text as Non-text while failing to correctly catch Trash. |

#### **Precision, Recall, and Distributional Divergence Algorithms**

To provide deeper analytical insight beyond simple volume metrics, the evaluation loop calculates advanced statistical and information-theoretic metrics:
**Macro and Weighted ![][image5] Scores:** The ![][image5] score is the harmonic mean of precision and recall, serving as a critical measure of a classification system's accuracy, particularly when dealing with highly imbalanced datasets (where Clear text drastically outnumbers Non-text). By computing both macro (the unweighted mean per class) and weighted (the mean proportional to specific class volume) ![][image5] scores, the developers can assess whether a configuration change actually improves the detection of minority classes—like rare structural Non-text elements or highly specific archival codes—without inadvertently degrading the accuracy of the majority Clear texts.4
**Kullback-Leibler (KL) Divergence Shift:** To mathematically measure how fundamentally a configuration change alters the overall macroscopic distribution of quality across the entire corpus, the tool utilizes Kullback-Leibler (KL) divergence.4 In information theory, KL divergence measures how one probability distribution (in this case, the baseline category distribution) differs from a second, reference probability distribution (the new experimental category distribution).
A calculated KL shift nearing zero strongly implies that the configuration change had negligible impact on the overall macroscopic distribution of document quality. Conversely, a high KL shift indicates a radical, systemic restructuring of how the pipeline perceives document quality as a whole. Monitoring the KL shift provides the engineering team with a single, highly reliable, and mathematically sound gauge of systemic volatility during rapid parameter tuning, ensuring that minor tweaks do not inadvertently destroy the statistical integrity of the entire corpus.4

### **Downstream LLM Dependencies and vLLM Architectural Constraints**

The intricate, deeply optimized post-processing mechanisms detailed within the atrium-alto-postprocess repository do not exist in an academic vacuum; they act as a non-negotiable foundational layer for broader systemic goals within the ATRIUM project. The urgency surrounding the optimization strategies and surrogate modeling detailed in Issue \#5 is highly contextualized by impending administrative deadlines. Specifically, the development loop orchestrated to resolve these bottlenecks is explicitly assigned to the "Q1-Q2" milestone.6 The overarching success of this mid-project beta heavily relies on the system's ability to seamlessly ingest, process, and accurately categorize historical text without buckling under computational load, necessitating the rapid, effective resolution of hyperparameter bottlenecks via the surrogate modeling framework.
Furthermore, the strictness of the text categorization—specifically the aggressive filtering of Trash and Non-text—is entirely dictated by the severe hardware limitations and behavioral quirks of the advanced Large Language Models operating in the downstream atrium-nlp-enrich repository. Discussions originating from related repositories (specifically atrium-nlp-enrich Issue \#6) reveal critical, ongoing optimizations regarding which LLMs to deploy for the final knowledge processing and keyword extraction phases.6
Extensive architectural testing indicates that models falling below the 8-Billion parameter threshold suffer heavily from catastrophic "context bleeding" and severe hallucination when dealing with highly specific historical, archeological, and cultural heritage terminology.6 These smaller models simply lack the parameter depth to correctly interpret subtle morphological variances in digitized texts, often hallucinating entirely new words when confronted with minor OCR noise.
Consequently, the current structural recommendation for production-level semantic extraction relies on the massive Qwen 3.6-27B model. This model successfully mitigates hallucinations and context bleeding while remaining barely viable on a single A100 or A40 GPU server node.6 For highly specialized scenarios demanding maximum theoretical precision—particularly in the complex categorization of archaeological burial types and specific find-type categorizations—the even larger Gemma 4-31B architecture is prioritized, albeit at the cost of vastly increased VRAM overhead that strains the server architecture.6 For highly resource-constrained nodes, the Qwen 3.5-9B model serves as the absolute bottom baseline, representing the only sub-14B architecture capable of managing the specialized context without severe data bleeding.6 These operational challenges are further compounded by ongoing server maintenance issues, as the project's GPU drivers are noted as being outdated for the newer vLLM 0.8+ inference servers, requiring careful memory management.6
The massive GPU resources and VRAM capacities required to host 27B and 31B parameter models downstream retroactively validate the incredibly strict computational governance occurring in the ALTO XML post-processing phase. By actively, aggressively filtering Trash and Non-text elements, and utilizing the highly compressed, hyper-efficient Qwen2.5-0.5B model strictly for perplexity scoring prior to final categorization 4, the atrium-alto-postprocess pipeline ensures that the incredibly expensive, highly constrained VRAM cycles of the larger downstream LLMs are never wasted attempting to extract knowledge from fundamentally irrecoverable OCR noise.

### **Systemic Outcomes and Future Viability**

The atrium-alto-postprocess architecture represents a highly advanced, ruthlessly optimized, and practically minded solution to the perennial challenges of ALTO XML data extraction and historical OCR degradation within the cultural heritage sector. By executing a sophisticated tri-modal extraction methodology—perfectly balancing the blazing, memory-efficient speed of CPU-bound XML parsing against the deep spatial geometry of LayoutReader and the profound visual intelligence of the GLM-4v-9b fallback model—the system ensures maximum operational flexibility across wildly varying and deeply degraded document topographies.
Its most significant architectural triumph lies in its rigorous implementation of asymmetric computational routing. By isolating neural inference strictly to a single, dedicated GPU worker utilizing a highly compressed perplexity model, while simultaneously deploying a massive 32-thread CPU phalanx to manage structural heuristics and fast-vector FastText language identification, the pipeline effectively neutralizes the severe hardware bottlenecks that historically cripple large-scale archival processing. Furthermore, its rigorous, multi-vector approach to textual categorization—synthesizing spatial geometry, linguistic perplexity, and character-level distributions into a unified, probabilistic quality metric—guarantees that downstream semantic translation and enrichment engines receive only high-fidelity, structurally coherent data streams.
However, the pipeline's extreme operational complexity inherently produces significant hyperparameter rigidity. The extensive tensor calculations and coordinate math required to generate the underlying features for the quality\_score render standard grid-search tuning methodologies mathematically unfeasible on available hardware. The strategic resolution proposed via the implementation of a vectorized, CPU-bound surrogate evaluation loop that relies entirely on immutable, pre-computed CSV feature matrices is an elegant, mathematically sound, and absolutely necessary engineering pivot. By permanently separating the high-speed categorization arithmetic from the agonizingly slow neural extraction phase, the system allows for the instantaneous calculation of vital performance metrics like KL divergence, flip rates, and harmonic ![][image5] shifts. This enables rapid, highly data-driven optimization of the configuration constants using standard developer hardware.
As the project continues to deeply integrate into the broader ATRIUM WP4 and WP5 infrastructure, facing strict administrative deadlines and the unforgiving hardware realities of hosting 31B parameter models, this newly engineered capacity for high-speed, offline parameter tuning will be the deciding factor in maintaining long-term pipeline stability. By ensuring the flawlessly accurate, rapidly tunable pre-filtering of historical data, the post-processing framework preserves the immensely valuable computational bandwidth required for the sophisticated, large-scale language models operating at the absolute zenith of the knowledge representation stack.

---

### Interpretation

Baseline is `macro_f1=1.0000` — the current config already classifies all 1,463 scored lines correctly. Importance scores reflect **sensitivity**: how much classification quality degrades when a parameter deviates from its current value. This is the signal for which constants need careful future calibration vs which are safe to tune freely.

**High sensitivity (handle with care):**
- `MOSTLY_READABLE_VALID_MIN` — dominant across all backends (perm. importance ~0.55). Controls the noisy/clear boundary for the largest share of the dataset; small shifts have outsized effect.
- `LOWPPL_CLEAR_MAX` — second-most influential; governs the low-perplexity clear threshold.
- `CATEG_GARBAGE_DENSITY_HIGH` — third; garbage density gate with consistent RF/Morris/Sobol agreement.
- `LOWPPL_CZECH_CLEAR_MAX` — fourth; Czech-specific clear path with elevated nonlinear influence in Sobol.

**Low sensitivity (safe to adjust freely):** most rotation/ghost/page-level parameters. `WEIRD_RATIO_INVERTED_MIN`, `GHOST_DOMINATED_MIN_RATIO`, `SUSPICIOUS_WQX_RATIO`, `INVERTED_WEIRD_PENALTY`, `GHOST_HITS_INVERTED_MIN` all score near zero across backends.

---
